GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 50.01 CONTRACT; TERMINATION REGULATIONS.
   (A)   The rules, regulations and water rates set out in this chapter shall
be considered a part of the contract with every person, company or corporation
which is supplied water through the water system of the town and every such
person, company or corporation by taking water shall be considered to express
his or her assent to be bound thereby and whenever any water rule or regulation
enacted by this chapter or hereinafter enacted by the town is violated, the
Superintendent of Waterworks is empowered to terminate the supply of water from
the property where the violation occurs; provided, the customer is given an
opportunity to review the nature of the violation with the Superintendent of
Waterworks prior to termination.
   (B)   If two or more parties receive a supply of water through the same
service pipe, a termination of service may still occur.
   (C)   Any charge for termination of service shall be charged to the property
as a bill for water used.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.010) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913; Ord. 82-8, passed - -1982)
§ 50.02 RULES AND REGULATIONS GENERALLY.
   The rules and regulations set out in this chapter for the government of
consumers, and any persons who may be legally authorized to put in waterworks
attachments, are adopted and established.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.020) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.03 SUPERINTENDENT OF WATERWORKS.
   The Board of Trustees shall appoint a Superintendent of Waterworks who shall
have general supervision of the waterworks, of all repairs and improvements
made on same and of the enforcement of all rules and regulations governing the
waterworks service.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.030) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.04 WATER RATES.
   Monthly rates and charges are established by resolution of the Board of
Trustees and the Board of Trustees, by resolution, may increase or reduce the
rates or change the charges when it determines that the scheduled charge is
inequitable or improper.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.040) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913; Ord. 52, passed - -1917;
Ord. 186, passed - -1962; Ord. 203, passed - -1969; Ord. 74-2, passed - -1974;
Ord. 78-20, passed - -1978; Ord. 81-2, passed - -1981; Ord. 94-1, passed - -
1994)
§ 50.05 YARD SPRINKLER USE PROHIBITED DURING FIRE ALARM.
   During all alarms of fire and while the fire pressure is on the main, the
use of any hose or any yard or street sprinkler is positively prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.380) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.06 RATES BASED ON CONSUMPTION.
   The rates set out in this chapter shall be based on monthly consumption
through one meter, and no combinations or readings from separate meters will be
allowed.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.060) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.07 CONTRACTORS AND BUILDERS.
   (A)   Contractors, builders and others desiring water for building purposes,
must make application to the Superintendent of the Waterworks therefor, who
will issue a permit.
   (B)   The amount paid therefor shall be based on the rate set out in this
chapter, or on any rate decided by the Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.070) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.08 STREET; WATERING PERIODS.
   Watering periods are from 6:00 a.m. to 8:00 p.m. East and north sides of
streets and avenues shall be watered on even days (i.e., Tuesdays, Thursdays
and Saturdays) and west and south sides of streets and avenues shall be watered
on odd days (i.e., Mondays, Wednesdays and Fridays) and that position of water
tap shall determine the time of watering.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.080) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913; Ord. 52, passed - -1917;
Ord. 186, passed - -1962)
§ 50.09 WATER TAPS; PROHIBITION AND CHARGE; AUTHORITY AND TOWN DUTIES.
   (A)   No water taps shall be made by anyone other than the town, and there
shall be a charge established by resolution of the Board of Trustees, and the
Board of Trustees, by resolution, may increase or reduce the rates or change
the charges when it determines that the scheduled charge is inequitable or
improper.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.090)
   (B)   (1)   The Superintendent of Waterworks shall have charge of tapping
the water mains and he or she shall have charge of and be responsible for the
tapping machine and all supplies used in and about the waterworks system
purchased by the town.
      (2)   The town will furnish all pipe and appurtenances required in
tapping the water mains and water meters, and bring the pipe to the outside
line of the sidewalk, for the sum of $30 for each tap, which includes the price
of the meter.
      (3)   The water connection will be made by the town upon application by
the water consumers in the order of the applications.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.100)
(Ord. 43, passed - -1913; Ord. 58, passed - -1918; Ord. 186, passed - -1962;
Ord. 94-1, passed - -1994)
§ 50.10 PLUMBER’S PERMIT AND BOND; RETURN AND REFUND.
   (A)   Every plumber shall, before making any connections with any main or
doing any work on any service pipes connected therewith, give to the town a
bond in the penal sum of $500, with good and sufficient surety, conditioned,
that he or she will in all things well and truly comply with all the rules and
regulations of the town for the government of plumbers.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.110)
   (B)   (1)   Within two days after the completion of any connections to the
main, returns shall be made upon the blanks as provided for the purpose.
      (2)   In case any permit remains unreturned for 30 days after the issue,
then the Superintendent shall refuse to grant any further permits to the town
plumber until the proper returns have been made.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.120) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.11 TAPPING OR CONNECTING TO WATER MAIN REQUIREMENTS.
   No person, except the plumbers having special permits from the
Superintendent, Board of Trustees or person in their service and approved by
them, will be permitted, under any circumstances to tap the water main, and the
kind and the size of the connections with the mains shall be specified in the
permits.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.130) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.12 TEST PIPE.
   Only plumbers and other approved persons shall admit water to test pipes and
shall do so for that purpose only.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.140) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.13 TURNING OFF WATER; REQUIREMENTS.
   Any plumber shutting off water from any property, except for a few days’
repairs, shall report to the Superintendent in writing.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.150) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.14 SERVICE PIPES; FLUSHING AND METER INSTALLATION; LAYING.
   (A)   Service pipes must be thoroughly flushed before meters are attached
and space left and prepared in an approved location for the attachments of
meter and connections.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.160)
   (B)   All service pipes must be laid at least four feet deep.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.170)
(Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.15 CORPORATION COCK.
   A corporation cock shall be inserted in every tap on the water mains. The
corporation cap shall be of a standard make and of pattern and weight approved
by the Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.180) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.16 STOP COCK.
   There shall be a stop cock in every service connection to the main, lateral
or extensions service, supply, in streets, within the parking near the curbline
and in alleys within one foot of the alley line.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.190) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.17 CURB COCK.
   The curb cock shall be covered by a three-inch extension stop box of a
standard pattern, extending to or lightly above grade and provided with a
tight-fitting iron cover with the word “water” or the letter “W” cast on the
cover.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.200) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.18 ONE HOUSE PER TAP; EXCEPTION.
   Not more than one house shall be supplied from one tap, except by special
permission of the Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.220) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.19 PIPE INSPECTION BEFORE COVERING.
   Before any pipe is covered, it shall be subject to inspection by Water
Superintendent or inspector, from the main to the meter.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.280) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.20 BARRICADING.
   (A)   No person shall leave any excavation made in the street or the highway
open at any time without barricading, and during the night time lights must be
maintained at such excavations.
   (B)   In making repairs, the sidewalks, the paving or bricks and earth
removed, must be deposited in such a manner that it will occasion the least
inconvenience to the public and provide for the passage of water along the
gutters.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.290) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.21 STOP AND WASTE COCK.
   There shall be a stop and waste cock of standard make and pattern and
weight, approved by the Board of Trustees of the town, attached to every
service pipe at the point where it enters the building, inside the same, so as
to admit of the water being shut off in freezing weather and the pipe and meter
drained.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.300) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.22 AUTHORITY TO ACCESS FROM PIPELINE TO METER TO MAIN; WATER WASTAGE
NOTICE; SHUT OFF.
   The town shall at all times be regarded and considered in possession of
service pipes from the main to the water and the Superintendent of the
Waterworks and such person or persons as may be directed by him or her shall
have authority to enter and have full access to the pipeline from the meter to
the main for the purpose of examining the same and, in case he or she finds
that water is wasting on account of negligence or for the want of repair, he or
she shall leave notice thereof and if such waste is not remedied within 24
hours thereafter, the water shall be turned off and shall not be turned on.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.310) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.23 SUSPENSION AUTHORITY OF USE FOR FOUNTAINS OR SPRINKLING.
   The right is reserved to suspend the use of the fountains and hose for
sprinkling streets, lawns, yards or gardens, whenever, in the opinion of the
Superintendent of Waterworks or Board of Trustees, the public exigency requires
it.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.320) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.24 UPKEEP OF WATER APPARATUS REQUIRED.
   All persons using water shall keep the hydrant, tap, hose, water closets,
urinals, baths or other fixtures in good repair, and shall be responsible for
any damage or injury resulting to others from the improper use or waste of
water.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.330) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.25 WATER SERVICE OUTSIDE TOWN LIMITS.
   The town may provide water service to property outside the town limits
subject to the following terms and conditions.
   (A)   An applicant requesting water service outside the town limits shall
enter into a water service contract with the town.
   (B)   (1)   An applicant requesting water service to any area where town
distribution and transmission facilities do not exist must pay the full costs
of extending utility lines to serve his or her property, including any costs
for appurtenant facilities such as storage and pumping stations.
      (2)   Upon completion of the work and written acceptance by the town, the
water distribution system will become the property of the town.
      (3)   The applicant is also responsible for obtaining and dedicating to
the town all easements required for the utility facilities.
   (C)   Rates for water service outside the town limits shall be two times the
rate for water service inside the town limits.
   (D)   (1)   Applicants for outside water service shall apply to the town for
a water tap and shall pay a water tap fee to the town in an amount established
by resolution of the Board of Trustees.
      (2)   Unless otherwise agreed in writing, the town will be responsible
for tapping the water main, running the service line from the water main to the
meter pit or curb stop and installing the meter pit and curb stop valve.
      (3)   The service line from the meter pit or curb stop to the structure
to be served shall be installed by the water user at his or her expense.
   (E)   A water meter is required for any building or residence with a service
line larger than three-quarters of an inch.
   (F)   Requests for commercial, industrial and non-residential water service
are subject to approval by the Board of Trustees on a case-by-case basis.
   (G)   Use of water outside the limits of the town shall be subject to the
paramount rights of users within the town limits. If there is insufficient
water to provide for users both within and without the town limits, the town
may reduce, curtail or shut off the users outside the town limits during such
period of water shortage or scarcity.
   (H)   Water service outside of the town limits is limited to properties
within the perimeter of the following county roads: CR 3 west of town; CR 28
south of town; CR 7 east of town; and CR 32 north of town.
   (I)   The terms and conditions of this section shall not apply to any
customer who as of the effective date of this section is already receiving
water service from the town for a property located outside the town limits, but
they shall apply once the subject property is sold or otherwise transferred.
(Ord. 2020-6, passed 12-7-2020)
§ 50.26 UPKEEP OF SERVICE PIPES AND OTHER APPARATUS REQUIRED.
   (A)   All persons taking the water shall keep their own service pipes, stop
and waste cocks, and other apparatus, in good repair at their own risk and
expense, and prevent unnecessary waste.
   (B)   In case service pipes, stop cocks, stop boxes or any other apparatus
connected herewith, get out of order or the stop boxes which hereafter may
become covered up so they cannot be seen readily, then the Superintendent of
Waterworks is authorized to repair and place same in proper condition, and
charge the same to the property as a bill for water used, reporting same to the
Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.350) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.27 RIGHT RESERVED TO CUT OFF WATER SUPPLY.
   (A)   It is expressly stipulated that no claim shall be made against the
town by reason of the breaking of any service cock or if from any cause the
supply of water should fail or from damage arising from shutting off the water
to repair mains, make connections or extensions, or for any purpose that may be
deemed necessary.
   (B)   The right is reserved to cut off the supply of water at any time,
notwithstanding any permit to the contrary.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.360) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.28 UNAUTHORIZED USE OF FIRE HYDRANTS PROHIBITED.
   No firefighter or other person, except for the legitimate purpose of
extinguishing fire or upon drill, shall open any fire hydrant or stop connected
with the fire drill service without the consent of the Superintendent of the
Waterworks.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.370) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913) Penalty, see §
50.99
WATER METERS
§ 50.45 METERS REQUIRED.
   A water meter, the property of the consumers, shall be attached to every
service pipe and placed in a position at the expense of the property owner, by
any qualified plumber working under the direction of the Superintendent of the
Waterworks, which meter shall be furnished the water consumer by the town at
actual cost.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.220) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.46 TESTING.
   When meters are attached to service pipes at least ten cubic feet of water
shall be run through the meter in order to ascertain if the same is in working
order and the readings as shown thereafter appear on the returns.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.230) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.47 RELOCATION ORDER.
   (A)   The Superintendent of the Waterworks may order the relocation of any
meter which is not now located in a proper, handy and accessible place, and
shut off the water in case of failure to relocate the same within ten days as
directed by the Superintendent of the Waterworks.
   (B)   All meters shall be so placed that they shall be easily accessible at
all times to meter readers and care must be taken not to cover them with wood,
coal or any material whatever.
   (C)   If, however, they should be inaccessible, or covered, then the
Superintendent of Waterworks may order the water turned off at the expense of
the property owner.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.240) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.48 PERMISSION REQUIRED FOR RELOCATION.
   The location of the water meter, owned by the consumer, shall not be changed
without permission of the Superintendent in writing.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.250) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.49 REPAIR REQUIRED; AUTHORITY TO SHUT OFF WATER.
   If any meter becomes out of repair or fails to work properly in the opinion
of the Superintendent of the Waterworks, then the Superintendent shall notify
the consumers to repair the same and, if the consumer fails to have such
repairs made within a reasonable time, then the Superintendent may cut off the
supply of water until such repairs are made and, for the time that such meter
has been out of repairs, the consumers shall pay the average of the last
reading of such meter before becoming out of repair.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.260) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.50 CHARGE ANY WATER PASSING THROUGH METER.
   All water passing through the meter will be charged for whether it is used
or not.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.270) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)
§ 50.99 PENALTY.
   Any person who does or performs any act or thing prohibited by this chapter
or otherwise than in accordance with its provisions, or violates any or either
of the rules or regulations, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, on
conviction therefor, in addition to the enforcement of the forfeitures,
liabilities, stipulations and reservations, shall be fined in the sum of not
more than $100.
(Prior Code, § 13.04.390) (Ord. 43, passed - -1913)

WASTEWATER ACTIVITY ENTERPRISE
§ 51.01 DECLARATION AND CREATION.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees finds and determines that it will provide
wastewater facilities and services by means of the town’s wastewater activity
enterprise in conformity with all applicable state laws.
   (B)   The Board of Trustees further:
      (1)   Recognizes and confirms that the Enterprise is an “enterprise”
within the meaning of the TABOR; and
      (2)   Declares its intent that the Enterprise be operated and maintained
so as to exclude its activities from the application of TABOR.
   (C)   Therefore, the Board of Trustees creates the “Town of Haxtun,
Colorado, Wastewater Activity Enterprise”. The Board of Trustees shall take all
actions on behalf of the Enterprise as hereinafter further provided.
(Ord. 4-2006, Series 2006, passed 11-30-2006)
§ 51.02 GOVERNING BOARD.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees of the town shall constitute the governing board
of the Enterprise (the “governing board”).
   (B)   The governing board shall conduct the business of the Enterprise in
the same manner and follow the same procedures as the Board of Trustees of the
town.
   (C)   All official business of the Enterprise shall be conducted at
regularly scheduled or special meetings of the Board of Trustees.
   (D)   The record of the proceedings of the governing board may be
incorporated in the minutes of the Board of Trustees and shall not be required
to be recorded separately.
   (E)   No additional oath of office, qualification or procedure shall apply
with respect to service as a member of the governing board.
   (F)   All business and actions of the governing board shall be governed by
and made subject to all requirements, privileges, immunities, protections,
limitations and other provisions of law.
(Ord. 4-2006, Series 2006, passed 11-30-2006)
§ 51.03 POWERS.
   (A)   The Enterprise shall exercise the powers of an enterprise under TABOR,
including, without limitation, the power to issue or reissue bonds, notes or
other obligations, payable from the revenues derived or to be derived from its
provision of services.
   (B)   The Enterprise shall also be entitled to exercise such powers as are
set forth in any applicable state law, including the power to set rates, fees
and charges for services provided by the Enterprise; provided, however, in no
event shall the Enterprise have the authority to levy or collect taxes, whether
sales taxes, use taxes or ad valorem taxes, nor shall the Enterprise have the
power to direct the town to exercise its taxing power on behalf of the
Enterprise.
(Ord. 4-2006, Series 2006, passed 11-30-2006)
§ 51.04 ASSETS.
   (A)   Assets to be operated and maintained by the Enterprise shall either
remain in the ownership of the town or be owned by the Enterprise, as the Board
of Trustees determines.
   (B)   The town assigns the use and management of all assets owned by the
town, whether real or personal, to the Enterprise.
   (C)   The Enterprise shall hold title to assets it owns in the name of the
“Town of Haxtun, Colorado acting by and through its Wastewater Activity
Enterprise”.
(Ord. 4-2006, Series 2006, passed 11-30-2006)
§ 51.05 ENTERPRISE FUND.
   (A)   An Enterprise Fund shall be established to separately account for all
revenues and expenditure incurred by the Enterprise.
   (B)   The Enterprise shall prepare an annual budget which may be included in
the budget prepared for the town.
   (C)   All budgets, reports, audits and financial operations of the
Enterprise shall conform to and be prepared in accordance with generally
accepted accounting principles applicable to governmental units and other
requirements of law.
(Ord. 4-2006, Series 2006, passed 11-30-2006)
§ 51.06 RATIFICATION AND APPROVAL OF PRIOR ACTIONS.
   All actions heretofore taken by the Mayor, any member of the Board of
Trustees, officers and employees of the town, not inconsistent with the
provisions of this subchapter, relating to the Enterprise, or actions to be
taken in respect thereof, are ratified, approved and confirmed.
(Ord. 4-2006, Series 2006, passed 11-30-2006)
CONDITIONS AND REGULATIONS
§ 51.20 SEWER CHARGE.
   The charges for the use of the town’s sewer system shall be as established
from time to time by resolution of the Board of Trustees, and the Board of
Trustees, by resolution, may increase or reduce the rates or change the charges
when it determines that the scheduled charge is inequitable or improper.
(Prior Code, § 13.08.010) (Ord. 187, passed - -1962; Ord. 204, passed - -1969;
Ord. 72-1, passed - -1972; Ord. 74-3, passed - -1974; Ord. 78-30, passed - -
1978; Ord. 79-1, passed - -1979; Ord. 81-1, passed - -1981; Ord. 94-1, passed -
-1994; Ord. 2019-3, passed 3-4-2019)
§ 51.21 SEWER TAPS.
   No sewer taps shall be made by anyone other than the town, and there shall
be a charge established by resolution of the Board of Trustees and the Board of
Trustees, by resolution, may increase or reduce the rates or change the charges
when it determines that the scheduled charge is inequitable or improper.
(Prior Code, § 13.08.020) (Ord. 187, passed - -1962; Ord. 94-1, passed - -1994)
§ 51.22 CHARGES FOR OUTSIDE PROPERTIES.
   The rates to be charged for use of the sewer system by properties situated
outside the boundaries of the town shall be established by resolution of the
Board of Trustees and the Board of Trustees, by resolution, may increase or
reduce the rates or change the charges when it determines that the scheduled
charge is inequitable or improper.
(Prior Code, § 13.08.030) (Ord. 187, passed - -1962; Ord. 94-1, passed - -1994)
§ 51.23 METHOD OF COLLECTION.
   (A)   (1)   All sewer rental charges shall be added to and made a part of
the monthly water rental bill and shall be paid in the same manner and shall be
subject to the same rules and regulations as provided for payment of other
water bills.
      (2)   The sewer rental charges shall also constitute a lien upon any
lots, land, building or premises served and, in the event the charges shall not
be paid when due, the service may be discontinued by the town by shutting off
the water supply from the premises; or the Town Clerk/Treasurer may certify the
charge or charges to the County Treasurer to be placed by him or her upon the
tax list for the current year to be collected in the manner as other taxes are
collected with 10% added thereto, to defray the cost of collection, and all
laws of the state for the assessment and collection of general taxes, including
the laws for the sale of property for taxes and redemption of the same shall
apply.
   (B)   Prior to termination of service provided, the customer shall be
provided notice and an opportunity to dispute the charges to the Superintendent
or such person’s designee.
(Prior Code, § 13.08.040) (Ord. 187, passed - -1962; Ord. 82-5, passed - -1982)
§ 51.24 RECONNECTING OWN SYSTEM AFTER TOWN’S DISCONNECTION PROHIBITED.
   It is unlawful, after sewer service has been discontinued by shutting off
the water supply or in any other manner, for the person to reconnect the same
without the consent of the town.
(Prior Code, § 13.08.050) (Ord. 187, passed - -1962) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.25 REPAIR/RETAP SEWER LINES AND TAPS.
   (A)   When it is deemed necessary to replace or repair a tap off of the main
sewer line, the following procedures will be followed: the owner of the tap
will notify the town that a sewer tap needs replaced or repaired.
   (B)   Responsibilities of the property owner are as follows:
      (1)   Notification - Utility Notification Center of Colorado;
      (2)   Procuring digging equipment and personnel to complete the project
will be done with the Town Superintendent or designee’s approval;
      (3)   If a tap needs replaced, the town will replace or repair the tap at
the property owner’s expense;
      (4)   If ditch is to be covered by cement or asphalt, the ditch will be
replaced with fill gravel, to minimize settling. If not covered by asphalt or
cement, the original fill may be replaced, but must be compacted to the
satisfaction of the Town Superintendent or designee. This work will be done at
the property owner’s expense;
      (5)   Curb and gutter, cement or asphalt replacement will be at the
property owner’s expense. This work will be completed within 30 days of project
start date; and
      (6)   Backfill, cement and asphalt replacement will be completed to the
satisfaction of the Town Superintendent or designee.
(Ord. 13.08, Series 2003, passed 5-5-2003)
§ 51.26 BARRICADING.
   (A)   No person shall leave any excavation made within the town at any time
without barricading.
   (B)   In making repairs, all debris, cement, asphalt and the like must be
deposited in such a manner that it will cause the least inconvenience to the
public and provide no hazards to the sewer system.
(Ord. 13.08, Series 2003, passed 5-5-2003) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.27 BACKFLOW APPARATUS AND CLEAN OUT.
   All backflow apparatus and cleanouts installed by the property owner will be
located on the owner’s property.
(Ord. 13.08, Series 2003, passed 5-5-2003) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.28 SEWERS CONNECTION.
   Sewer connection, apparatus, taps and the like will be installed in
accordance with the latest edition of the Uniform Plumbing Code of the
International Association of Plumbing and Mechanical Officials.
(Ord. 13.08, Series 2003, passed 5-5-2003)
§ 51.29 UNLAWFUL DISCHARGE OF POLLUTANTS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit the introduction of any one or
more of the following pollutants into the town’s sewer system from any source
of non-domestic discharge:
   (A)   Pollutants which create a fire or explosion hazard in the town’s sewer
system, including, but not limited to, waste streams with a closed cup
flashpoint of less than 60°C (140°F) using the test methods specified in 40
C.F.R. § 261.21;
   (B)   Pollutants which will cause corrosive structural damage to the town’s
sewer system, but in no case discharges with a pH of lower than 5.0 standard
units unless the treatment facilities are specifically designed to accommodate
such discharges;
   (C)   Solid or viscous pollutants in amounts which will cause obstruction to
the flow in the town’s sewer system, or otherwise interfere with the sewer
system’s operation;
   (D)   Any pollutant, including oxygen demanding pollutants (e.g., BODs),
released in a discharge at a flow rate and/or pollutant concentration which
will cause interference with any treatment process of town treatment
facilities;
   (E)   Heat in amounts which will inhibit biological activity in the town’s
sewer system resulting in interference, but in no case heat in such quantities
that the temperature at the town’s treatment facilities exceeds 40°C (104°F)
unless the state’s Department of Public Health and Environment, upon request of
the town, approves alternative temperature limits;
   (F)   Petroleum oil, non-biodegradable cutting oil or products of mineral
oil origin in amounts that will cause interference or pass through;
   (G)   Pollutants which result in the presence of toxic gases, vapors or
fumes within the town’s sewer system in a quantity that may cause acute worker
health and safety problems;
   (H)   Any trucked or hauled pollutants, except at discharge points
designated by the town; and/or
   (I)   Any other pollutant which may cause pass through or interference.
(Ord. 2019-3, passed 3-4-2019) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
(Prior Code, § 13.08.050) (Ord. 187, passed - -1962)
CHAPTER 52: CROSS-CONNECTION CONTROL
Section
   
52.01   Building plans
   
52.02   Backflow prevention assemblies; standards; approval
   
52.03   Installation compliance
   
52.04   Testing and maintenance
   
52.05   Right of entry
   
52.06   Violations
§ 52.01 BUILDING PLANS.
   (A)   All building plans must be submitted to the town and approved, prior
to the issuance of water service.
   (B)   Building plans must show:
      (1)   Water service type, size and location;
      (2)   Meter size and location;
      (3)   Backflow prevention assembly size, type and location;
      (4)   Fire sprinkling system(s) service line, size and type of backflow
prevention assembly if applicable;
      (5)   Backflow prevention assembles are to be installed in an accessible
location to facilitate maintenance, testing and repair. Drawings must show
various installations;
      (6)   All backflow prevention assembles shall be installed immediately
downstream of the water meter;
      (7)   Before installing a backflow prevention assembly, pipelines should
be thoroughly flushed to remove foreign materials;
      (8)   In no case will it be permissible to have connections or tees
between the meter and service line backflow prevention assembly;
      (9)   Backflow prevention valves are not to be used as the inlet or out
valve of the water meter. Test cocks are not to be used as supply connections
(not applied to residential dual check installations);
      (10)   In order to ensure that backflow prevention assembles continue to
operate satisfactorily, it will be necessary that they be tested at the time of
installation and on an annual schedule thereafter. Such test will be conducted
in accordance with ASSE and/or USC-CCC & HR performance standards and field
test procedures as directed by the state’s Department of Public Health and
Environment (not applied to residential dual check installations; dual checks
will be tested at intervals set by the Board);
      (11)   The town will require inspection of all containment installations;
      (12)   All costs for design, installation, maintenance, repair and
testing are to be borne by the customer;
      (13)   No grandfather clause exists. All laws and regulations apply
regardless of the age of the facility;
      (14)   All fire sprinkling lines shall have a minimum protection of an
approved double check valve for containment of the system;
      (15)   All glycol (ethylene or propylene) or antifreeze systems shall
have an approved reduced pressure zone assembly for containment;
      (16)   Dry fire systems shall have an approved double check valve
installed upstream of the air pressure valve;
      (17)   Single-family residence with a fire sprinkler system and domestic
water combined shall have a double check valve when no chemicals are used; and
      (18)   All fire sprinkler systems shall conform to the following sections
of the National Fire Protection Association Standard 13 and 25.
(Ord. 13.06, Series 2003, passed 2-17-2003)
§ 52.02 BACKFLOW PREVENTION ASSEMBLIES; STANDARDS; APPROVALS.
   (A)   (1)   Any backflow prevention assembly required herein shall be of a
model and size approved by the town.
      (2)   The term APPROVED BACKFLOW PREVENTION ASSEMBLY shall mean an
assembly that has been manufactured in full conformance with the standards
established by the latest version of the state’s Department of Public Health
and Environment Cross-Connection Control Manual and by the town.
      (3)   Final approval shall be evidence by a certificate of approval
issued by an approved testing laboratory certifying full compliance with State
Department of Public Health and Environment standards and ASSE or USC-FCCC and
HR specifications.
   (B)   Only approved backflow prevention assembles shall be used.
      (1)   The following testing laboratories are qualified to test and
certify backflow prevention assembles and being listed on their periodic
approved list shall meet all of the above requirements:
         (a)   American Society of Sanitary Engineering (ASSE), 901 Canterbury,
Suite A, Westlake, OH 44145; and
         (b)   USC Foundation for Cross-Connection Control and Hydraulic
Research, University of Southern California, KAP-200 University Park MC-2531,
Los Angeles, CA 90089-2531. Exception: Residential containment may be
accomplished with an assembly not approved by the Foundation for Cross-
Connection Control and Hydraulic Research, but approved by the American Society
of Sanitary and Mechanical Engineers and designated by the town.
      (2)   Backflow preventers currently installed which are not approved
shall be replaced with an approved assembly at the time they fail an
operational test.
      (3)   Backflow assembles used on fire lines shall have O.S.& Y. (outside
stem and yoke) valves and be listed by the National Fire Protection
Association.
(Ord. 13.06, Series 2003, passed 2-17-2003)
§ 52.03 INSTALLATION COMPLIANCE.
   Backflow prevention assemblies shall be installed in accordance with the
town.
   (A)   Backflow prevention assembly installations shall be inspected and
approved use by the town.
   (B)   All backflow assembles shall be installed in the horizontal position.
Vertical installation shall be acceptable when approved by ASSE or UCS-FCCC &
HR specifications. Variance may be granted by review.
   (C)   A pressure vacuum breaker shall be used where the assembly is never
subjected to back-pressure and installed a minimum of 12 inches highest piping
or outlet downstream of the assembly in a manner to preclude back-pressure.
   (D)   An atmospheric vacuum breaker shall be used only where the assembly
is:
      (1)   Installed as an isolation assembly;
      (2)   Never subjected to continuous pressure (more than 12 hours
continuous); and
      (3)   Installed with the air inlet in a level position and a minimum of
six inches above the highest piping or outlet it is protecting.
   (E)   The single check valve is not considered a backflow prevention
assembly.
   (F)   Double check valve assemblies may be installed in below grade vaults
when these vaults are properly constructed in accordance with the town. They
must be insulated to prevent freezing.
   (G)   Reduced pressure backflow preventers will be installed above ground.
The unit should be placed at least 12 inches above the finish grade to allow
clearance for the repair work. A concrete slab at finish grade is recommended.
Proper drainage should be provided for the relief valve and may be piped away
from the location; provided, it is readily visible from above grade and
provided the relief valve is separated from the drain line by a minimum of
double the diameter of the supply line. A modified vault installation my be
used if constructed with ample side clearances. Freezing is a major problem in
this area. Precautions should be taken to protect above ground installations.
(Ord. 13.06, Series 2003, passed 2-17-2003)
§ 52.04 TESTING AND MAINTENANCE.
   (A)   (1)   At least once per year, it will be the duty of the customer/user
at any premises where any backflow prevention assembly(s) are installed to have
certified test made of these assemblies.
      (2)   In those specific instances where the town deems the hazard to be
great enough certified inspections and test at more frequent intervals may be
required. These tests shall be at the expense of the water user and shall be
performed by a certified technician approved by the state’s Department of
Public Health and Environment and the town.
      (3)   An inspection of the assembly may be performed at any time,
complying with §
52.06 of this chapter (not applicable to dual check installations).
   (B)   As necessary, the assembly shall be repaired or replaced at the
expense of the customer/user whenever the assembly(s) is found to be defective.
Records of all such tests, repairs or replacement shall be kept by customer/
user and the town.
   (C)   Existing assembles shall be sealed by the technician performing the
test at the completion of the test.
   (D)   All testing equipment used in testing of backflow prevention
assemblies shall be checked for accuracy yearly, or more often, and proof of
compliance shall be submitted to the town upon request.
   (E)   The town retains the right to test or otherwise check the installation
and operation of any containment assembly at any time to assure proper
operation.
(Ord. 13.06, Series 2003, passed 2-17-2003)
§ 52.05 RIGHT OF ENTRY.
   (A)   A representative of the town will carry proper credentials of his or
her office.
   (B)   By previously arranged appointment and upon presentation of proper
credentials, the town representative shall have the right of entry to inspect
any and all buildings and premises for cross-connections relative to possible
hazards. This right of entry shall be a condition of water service in order to
protect the health, safety and welfare of the people throughout the town’s
distribution system.
   (C)   Where building security is required, the backflow assembly(s) should
be located in an area not subject to security.
   (D)   Questions regarding proper credentials should be directed to the town.
(Ord. 13.06, Series 2003, passed 2-17-2003)
§ 52.06 VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   Failure of the customer to cooperate in the installation, maintenance,
testing or inspection of backflow prevention. Assembles required by this
chapter shall be grounds for the discontinuance of water service to the
premises or the requirement for an air-gap separation from the public potable
water system.
   (B)   Service of water to any premises may be discontinued by the town if
unprotected cross-connections exist on the premises. When any defect is found
in an installed backflow prevention assembly or, if backflow prevention
assembly has been removed or bypassed, the service may be discontinued. Service
shall not be restored until such conditions or defects are corrected.
   (C)   Discontinuance of service may be summary, immediate and without
written notice whenever, in the judgment of the town, such action is necessary
to protect the public potable water supply or the distribution system.
(Ord. 13.06, Series 2003, passed 2-17-2003)
CHAPTER 53: SOLID WASTE
Section
   
53.01   Definition
   
53.02   Trash disposal service compulsory
   
53.03   Premises excluded from service
   
53.04   Duty of contractors to clean premises
   
53.05   Private trash hauling
   
53.06   Charges established
   
53.07   Lien for unpaid bills
§ 53.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definition shall apply unless
the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   TRASH. All waste matter, rubbish, debris and discarded materials of every
kind, including by way of illustration and no limitation, wastepaper , tin
cans, letter, grass clippings, tree leaves, boxes and cold ashes. TRASH does
not include hot ashes, building materials, dirt, rocks, sod, furniture or
appliances.
(Ord. 2, Series 2002, passed 8-5-2002)
§ 53.02 TRASH DISPOSAL SERVICE COMPULSORY.
   (A)   The town, its contractor, or town licensed operators shall furnish a
trash collection and disposal service as provided herein for all persons
resident within the town, except those specifically excluded in §
53.03 of this chapter. This service shall be maintained under the supervision
of the Department of Public Works.
   (B)   The town, by and through its duly authorized employees, its
contractors or town licensed operator, shall be the sole agency for the
collection of trash within the town. No other person shall collect trash within
the town unless expressly authorized by the terms of this chapter.
(Ord. 2, Series 2002, passed 8-5-2002)
§ 53.03 EXCLUSIONS FROM SERVICE.
   Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, the town shall not collect
trash from those premises that require special equipment or containers,
hazardous material, asphalt siding or shingles, oil and tires.
(Ord. 2, Series 2002, passed 8-5-2002)
§ 53.04 DUTY OF CONTRACTORS TO CLEAN PREMISES.
   Nothing in this chapter shall relieve any contractor of the obligation of
cleaning up premises after completion of a contract.
(Ord. 2, Series 2002, passed 8-5-2002)
§ 53.05 PRIVATE TRASH HAULING.
   Nothing in this chapter shall prevent an individual from hauling the
individual’s own trash; providing, it is properly disposed of in conformity
with all town and county regulations; however, such individuals shall continue
to be responsible for paying all town trash disposal charges.
(Ord. 2, Series 2002, passed 8-5-2002)
§ 53.06 CHARGES ESTABLISHED.
   The charges for trash disposal service as provided herein shall be as
established from time to time by resolution of the Board of Trustees. Such
charges shall be added to and made a part of the monthly electric service bill
and shall be paid in the same manner as electric bills. The trash disposal
charges shall also constitute a lien upon any lots, and building or premises
served, and in the event the charges are not paid when due, the Town Clerk/
Treasurer may certify the charge or charges to the County Treasurer pursuant to
§
53.07 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2, Series 2002, passed 8-5-2002)
§ 53.07 LIEN FOR UNPAID BILLS.
   Until all charges for town trash disposal service have been paid, they shall
constitute a lien upon any lots, land, building or premises served, and in the
event the charges are not paid when due, the Town Clerk/Treasurer may certify
the charge or charges to the County Treasurer to be placed upon the tax list
for the current year to be collected in the manner as other taxes are collected
with 10% added thereto to defray the cost of collection, and all laws of the
state for the assessment and collection of general taxes, including the laws
for the sale of property for taxes and redemption of the same, shall apply.
(Ord. 2, Series 2002, passed 8-5-2002)

54.35   Disconnection charges
ELECTRICITY ACTIVITY ENTERPRISE
§ 54.01 DECLARATION AND CREATION.
   (A)   There is recognized, established and designated the “Town of Haxtun
Electric Utility Enterprise” (the “Enterprise”). The Board of Trustees finds
and determines that it will provide electric services by means of the
Enterprise in conformity with all applicable state laws.
   (B)   The Board of Trustees further:
      (1)   Recognizes and confirms that the Enterprise is an “enterprise”
within the meaning of the TABOR; and
      (2)   Declares its intent that the Enterprise be operated and maintained
so as to exclude its activities from the application of TABOR.
   (C)   The Board of Trustees shall take all actions on behalf of the
Enterprise as hereinafter further provided.
(Ord. 2023-5, passed 11-6-2023)
§ 54.02 GOVERNING BOARD.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees shall constitute the governing board of the
Enterprise (the “governing board”).
   (B)   The governing board shall conduct the business of the Enterprise in
the same manner and follow the same procedures as the Board of Trustees.
   (C)   All official business of the Enterprise shall be conducted at
regularly scheduled or special meetings of the Board of Trustees.
   (D)   It shall not be necessary for the governing body to meet separately
from the regular and special meetings and study sessions of the Board of
Trustees, nor shall it be necessary for the governing body to specifically
announce or acknowledge that actions taken thereby are taken by the governing
body of the Enterprise.
   (E)   The record of the proceedings of the governing board may be
incorporated in the minutes of the Board of Trustees and shall not be required
to be recorded separately.
   (F)   No additional oath of office, qualification or procedure shall apply
with respect to service as a member of the governing board.
   (G)   All business and actions of the governing board shall be governed by
and made subject to all requirements, privileges, immunities, protections,
limitations and other provisions of law.
(Ord. 2023-5, passed 11-6-2023)
§ 54.03 POWERS.
   (A)   The Enterprise shall exercise the powers of an Enterprise under TABOR,
including, without limitation, the power to issue or reissue bonds, notes or
other obligations, payable from the revenues derived or to be derived from its
provision of services.
   (B)   The Enterprise shall also be entitled to exercise such powers as are
set forth in any applicable state law, including the power to set rates, fees
and charges for services provided by the Enterprise; provided, however, in no
event shall the Enterprise have the authority to levy or collect taxes, whether
sales taxes, use taxes or ad valorem taxes, nor shall the Enterprise have the
power to direct the town to exercise its taxing power on behalf of the
Enterprise.
(Ord. 2023-5, passed 11-6-2023)
§ 54.04 ASSETS.
   (A)   Assets to be operated and maintained by the Enterprise shall either
remain in the ownership of the town or be owned by the Enterprise, as the Board
of Trustees determines.
   (B)   The town assigns the use and management of all assets owned by the
town, whether real or personal, to the Enterprise.
   (C)   The Enterprise shall hold title to assets it owns in the name of the
“Town of Haxtun, Colorado acting by and through its Electric Utility
Enterprise”.
(Ord. 2023-5, passed 11-6-2023)
§ 54.05 ENTERPRISE FUND.
   (A)   An Enterprise Fund shall be established to separately account for all
revenues and expenditure incurred by the Enterprise.
   (B)   The Enterprise shall prepare an annual budget which may be included in
the budget prepared for the town.
   (C)   All budgets, reports, audits and financial operations of the
Enterprise shall conform to and be prepared in accordance with generally
accepted accounting principles applicable to governmental units and other
requirements of law.
(Ord. 2023-5, passed 11-6-2023)
§ 54.06 RATIFICATION AND APPROVAL OF PRIOR ACTIONS.
   All actions heretofore taken by the Mayor, any member of the Board of
Trustees, officers and employees of the town, not inconsistent with the
provisions of this subchapter, relating to the Enterprise, or actions to be
taken in respect thereof, are ratified, approved and confirmed.
(Ord. 2023-5, passed 11-6-2023)

§ 54.21 RULES AND REGULATIONS GENERALLY.
   The rules and regulations forming a part of this subchapter shall govern the
use of electric service from the town’s Municipal Electric Plant.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.020) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.22 RULES, SCHEDULE AND REGULATIONS; FILING.
   The rate schedules and rules and regulations shall be filed with the Public
Utilities Commission of the state in accordance with the Public Utilities Act,
being C.R.S. § 40-1-103.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.030) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.23 BILLS PAYABLE WHERE.
   All bills are payable at the office of the Town Clerk/Treasurer as to an
authorized agent of the town.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.060) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.24 DISCOUNT PERIOD; FAILURE TO RECEIVE BILL NOT ENTITLEMENT.
   Failure to receive bill will not entitle consumer to any discounts provided
for in the rate schedules if the bill is not paid within the discount period.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.070) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.25 NON-PAYMENT OF BILL; DISCONNECTION AND COSTS.
   (A)   Any user of electric service from the municipal electric plant, who
shall fail or refuse to pay therefor on or before the close of business on the
twentieth day of each month, shall be disconnected by the Superintendent of the
Electric Light and Water Plant, and the service shall not be again connected
until all delinquent charges and the cost of disconnecting and reconnecting
shall be paid in full, together with such other charges or expenses as are or
may be incidental thereto, and the Superintendent of the Electric Light and
Water Plant shall remove the electric meter from the premises of any person who
shall fail or refuse to pay charges on or before 30 days after the first day of
each month.
   (B)   (1)   A disconnection fee of $30 will be added to all utility accounts
that are not paid by the twentieth day of each month, effective 12-1-2024.
      (2)   The disconnection fee will not be applied to utility account
balances made up of late fees.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.080) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.26 ELECTRICAL WIRING OF CONSUMER.
   (A)   The town shall deliver electrical energy at the point where the
service wires enter the consumer’s building and its responsibility shall
terminate at the delivery point.
   (B)   All wiring and other electrical equipment used on the premises in
connection with the town service shall be suitable for the purpose hereof and
shall be maintained by the consumer at all times in safe condition in
conformity with reasonable rules and regulations in force from time to time.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.100) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.27 NOTICE OF DISCONTINUANCE.
   Notice to discontinue the supply of electricity must be given in writing at
the office of the Town Clerk/Treasurer. The consumer will be responsible for
all electricity consumed until such notice is given and a reasonable time
allowed to take the final reading of the meter.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.110) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.28 METERING.
   Upon metering service the electricity consumed shall be measured by a meter
owned and installed by the town upon the premises and at a point convenient for
the town’s service and upon the registration of the meter all bills shall be
calculated.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.130) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.29 BILL DISPUTE AND RESOLUTION.
   Upon a disputed bill arising from the question of the accuracy of meters,
adjustment shall be made in accordance with the rules and regulations laid down
by the Public Utilities Commission of the state.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.140) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.30 ACCESS TO METERS.
   The town’s authorized agents shall have access to the consumer’s premises at
any reasonable hour for the purpose of:
      (1)   Seeing that meters are kept in proper condition;
      (2)   To ascertain the quantity of electricity consumed; to inspect the
consumer’s installation or to cut off the supply of electricity for non-payment
of bill when past due; or
      (3)   For infraction of these rules and regulations.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.150) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.31 NON-LIABILITY; SPECIFIC CASES.
   (A)   The town agrees to use reasonable diligence in providing regular and
uninterrupted supply of current, but in case the supply of current should be
interrupted or fail by any reason of accident, state or municipal interference
or any other cause whatsoever, the town shall not be liable for damages for
such interruption of failure.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.160)
   (B)   The town shall not be liable for damages resulting to the consumer or
to any third person from the use of electric current, or the presence of the
town’s appliances on the consumer’s premises, unless due to willful fault or
neglect on the part of the town.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.170)
(Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.32 RESERVATION OF CERTAIN RIGHTS.
   The town reserves the right to regulate and control the use of electricity
in any class of service so that it will not unduly interfere with other
electric service.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.180) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921)
§ 54.33 CONSUMERS; COMPLAINTS; RIGHT OF REVIEW BEFORE DISCONTINUANCE.
   (A)   The town requests the consumer to notify the Mayor of the town of any
insufficiency of supply or unsatisfactory service or any inattention or
discourtesy upon the part of its employees or agents.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.190)
   (B)   Prior to the discontinuance of the supply of electricity for failure
or refusal to pay for the electric service, the consumer shall be given an
opportunity to review all assessments and charges with the Superintendent of
the Electric Light and Water Plant. The review, if requested by the consumer,
shall be held no later than ten days prior to discontinuance of service.
(Prior Code, § 13.12.200) (Ord. 85, passed - -1921; Ord. 82-61, passed - -1982)
§ 54.34 CASH METER DEPOSITS.
   A cash deposit will be required for each electric meter. The amount of the
deposit will be set by resolution.
(Ord. 13.12.091, passed - -)
§ 54.35 DISCONNECTION CHARGES.
   Charges for reconnection of a service will be set by resolution.
(Ord. 13.12.091, passed - -)
CHAPTER 55: UTILITIES GENERALLY
Section
   
55.01   Responsibility for payment; delinquencies
§ 55.01 RESPONSIBILITY FOR PAYMENT; DELINQUENCIES.
   (A)   Responsibility for payment; lien.
      (1)   Regardless of the occupancy of a premises, the owner thereof shall
be responsible for payment of all electric, water, sewer and sanitation charges
arising out of provision of such services to the owner’s premises, or arising
out of any repair to or maintenance of the owner’s service connections. All
service charges, delinquent electric, water, sewer and sanitation charges,
together with penalties, interest and the cost of collection of the same, if
any, shall be and remain a lien upon the property to which the services are
delivered from the date such charges, penalties, service charges, together with
interest and any cost of collection, become due until the same are paid. This
lien against the property, or the liability against the owner, may be enforced
by the town by an action at law or an action to enforce the lien.
      (2)   In the event that any person in possession of any premises pays the
entire charges due and owing, the payment shall relieve the owner from such
liability and the premises from the lien; however, the town shall in no event
be required to look to any person other than the owner of the premises for the
payment of the charges. No change in ownership or occupation shall affect the
application of this section or any of its provisions and the failure of any
owner to learn that he or she purchased any property against which a lien for
electric, water, sewer or sanitation serves exists shall in no way affect his
or her liability for such payment in full or be the basis for any claim of any
kind whatsoever against the town for refusing to turn of electric, water, sewer
or sanitation services until such charges have been paid in full.
   (B)   Delinquencies; remedies. If any charge for electric, water, sewer or
sanitation service imposed pursuant to this public works title is not paid by
the date due, the town may avail itself of any or all combination of the
following remedies, in addition to any other available remedies.
      (1)   The town may foreclose the lien imposed by division (A) above in
accordance with law.
      (2)   The town may maintain an action in any court of competent
jurisdiction for the amount of the charges due and any interest, costs and
attorney fees allowed by law.
      (3)   The town may certify the amount of the charge due to the County
Clerk and Treasurer, together with the assessment fee provided by resolution,
to become an assessment upon the property served and to be collected and paid
over to the Town Clerk/Treasurer in the same manner as taxes.
(Ord. 2015-2, passed 4-6-2015)

§ 70.01 MODEL TRAFFIC CODE ADOPTED.
   (A)   Adoption. 
      (1)   Pursuant of C.R.S. Title 31, Art. 15, part 4 and Art. 16, parts 1
and 2 there is adopted Art. I and II, inclusive, of the 2003 edition of the
Model Traffic Code, promulgated and published as such by the state’s Department
of Transportation, Safety and Traffic Engineering Branch, 4201 East Arkansas
Avenue, EP 700, Denver, CO 80222.
      (2)   The subject matter of the Model Traffic Code relates primarily to
comprehensive traffic-control regulations for town.
      (3)   The purpose of this code of ordinances’ traffic code and the Code
adopted herein is to provide a system of traffic regulations consistent with
state law and generally conforming to similar regulations throughout the state
and the nation.
      (4)   Three copies of the Model Traffic Code adopted herein are now filed
in the office of the Clerk/Treasurer of the town and may be inspected during
regular business hours.
   (B)   Deletions. The 2003 edition of the Model Traffic Code is adopted as if
set out at length save and except the following articles and/or sections which
are declared to be inapplicable to the municipality and are therefore expressly
deleted: none.
   (C)   Additions or modifications. The said adopted Code is subject to the
following additions or modifications: none.
   (D)   Application. 
      (1)   This traffic code shall apply to every street, alley, sidewalk
area, driveway, park and to every other public way or public place or public
parking area, either within or outside the corporate limits of the
municipality, the use of which the municipality has jurisdiction and authority
to regulate.
      (2)   The provisions of §§ 1401, 1402, 1413 and part 16 of the adopted
Model Traffic Code, respectively concerning reckless driving, careless driving,
eluding a police officer and accidents and accident reports shall apply not
only to public places and ways, but also throughout the municipality.
   (E)   Interpretation. 
      (1)   This traffic code shall be so interpreted and construed as to
effectuate its general purpose of conforming to the state’s Uniform System for
the Regulation of Vehicles and Traffic.
      (2)   Article and section headings of the ordinance and adopted Model
Traffic Code shall not be deemed to govern, limit, modify or in any manner
affect the scope, meaning or extent of the provisions of any article or section
thereof.
(Ord. 2, Series 2004, passed 6-7-2004) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.02 OBSTRUCTING STREETS.
   It is unlawful for any person, persons, company, corporation or individual
owning or operating any railway car, railway train or other vehicle or vehicles
upon or across any street or public way within the town to so operate the same
that the free passage of ordinary vehicles and persons along or upon the street
or public way is obstructed for a longer period than ten minutes without
clearing the street or public way for the passage of such vehicles and persons.
(Prior Code, § 10.16.010) (Ord. 23, passed - -1910) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.03 STATE HIGHWAYS AND CONNECTING LINKS.
   (A)   Violating statutes within portions inside town unlawful. On no portion
of any state highway or connecting link within the town shall any person
violate any of the provisions of the Model Traffic Code, nor any of the laws
amending the same, or any of the rules or regulations issued in pursuance
thereof.
(Prior Code, § 10.20.010)
   (B)   Parking and prima facie speed limit.
      (1)   (a)   Parking is prohibited at those points along the portions of
the streets which are within 20 feet of any intersection.
         (b)   Parking, when and where permitted, shall be parallel as provided
by law for parallel parking.
      (2)   Upon the basis of engineering and traffic investigations by the
Department of Highways, and by the town, it has been determined that a
reasonable and true prima facie speed limit on portions of the streets shall be
a minimum of 35 mph in the business district and a minimum of 35 mph on the
remaining portions; provided that, standard signs are erected giving notice of
the authorized speed as provided by the Model Traffic Code.
(Prior Code, § 10.20.020)
   (C)   Certain streets to remain through streets.
      (1)   (a)   Portions of the streets, when constructed and improved, shall
remain through streets.
         (b)   The town acknowledges the right of the state’s Department of
Highways to place signs and warnings at points selected by the Department for
the purpose of informing the traveling public that the portions of the streets
are through streets, and for the purpose of requiring such stops and speeds and
other traffic controls as may be necessary to protect the traveling public in
the use of those portions of the streets.
      (2)   No commercial activity or encroachment shall be permitted within
the right-of-way boundaries of the streets, and the width from curb to curb of
the streets shall be a minimum of 60 feet.
(Prior Code, § 10.20.030)
   (D)   State highway parking prohibited. There shall be no parking whatsoever
on any roadway or contiguous shoulder of any state highway or connection link
within the town during the times and at the places where snow removal
operations are in progress.
(Prior Code, § 10.20.040)
   (E)   Required submission to state of traffic and parking regulations to be
adopted. All traffic and parking regulations hereafter adopted which pertain to
the streets and roadway which form a part of the State Highway System or are a
connecting link thereof, shall be submitted to the Department of Highways for
approval in accordance with the provisions of C.R.S. § 43-2-135 before they
shall become effective.
(Prior Code, § 10.20.050)
(Ord. 180, passed - -1960) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 70.99 PENALTY.
   The following penalties, herewith set forth in full, shall apply to this
traffic code.
   (A)   It is unlawful for any person to violate any of the provisions adopted
in this traffic code.
   (B)   Every person convicted of a violation of any provision adopted in this
traffic code shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $300.
(Prior Code, § 10.20.060) (Ord. 180, passed - -1960; Ord. 2, Series 2004,
passed 6-7-2004; Ord. 2020-2, passed 5-4-2020)
