BUILDING CODES
§ 150.01 UNIFORM BUILDING CODE ADOPTED.
   (A)   Pursuant to C.R.S. Title 31, Art. 16, part 2, there is adopted by
reference the Uniform Building Code, 1991 Edition, as published by the
International Conference of Building Officials, 5360 South Workman Mill Road,
Whittier, CA 90601, subject to any amendments set forth herein, to protect the
health, safety and general welfare by providing minimum standards for the
design, construction, quality of materials, use and occupancy, location and
maintenance of buildings and other structures.
   (B)   In case of any conflict between such code adopted herein and any other
specific provision of this municipal code, the specific provision of the
municipal code shall prevail.
(Prior Code, § 15.04.010) (Ord. 2017-2, passed 4-3-2017)
§ 150.02 UNIFORM HOUSING CODE ADOPTED.
   (A)   Pursuant to C.R.S. Title 31, Art. 16, part 2, there is adopted by
reference the Uniform Housing Code, 1991 Edition, as published by the
International Conference of Building Officials, 5360 South Workman Mill Road,
Whittier, CA 90601, subject to any amendments set forth herein, to protect and
safeguard life, limb, health, property and public welfare by regulating,
providing minimum standards, and controlling the use and occupancy, location
and maintenance of residential buildings and other structures within the town.
   (B)   In case of any conflict between such code adopted herein and any other
specific provision of this municipal code, the specific provision of the
municipal code shall prevail.
(Prior Code, § 15.08.010) (Ord. 2017-2, passed 4-3-2017)
§ 150.03 UNIFORM FIRE CODE.
   (A)   Pursuant to C.R.S. Title 31, Art. 16, part 2, there is adopted by
reference the Uniform Fire Code Standards, 1991 Edition, as published by the
International Conference of Building Officials, 5360 South Workman Mill Road,
Whittier, CA 90601 and the Western Fire Chiefs Association, 5360 South Workman
Mill Road, Whittier, CA 90601, subject to any amendments set forth herein, to
protect the public health, safety and welfare by providing minimum standards
relating to the storage, handling and use of hazardous substances, materials
and devices, and providing greater safety and protection to the public from
conditions hazardous to life or property in the occupancy of buildings or
premises.
   (B)   In case of any conflict between such code adopted herein and any other
specific provision of this municipal code, the specific provision of the
municipal code shall prevail.
(Prior Code, § 15.12.010) (Ord. 2017-2, passed 4-3-2017)
§ 150.04 NATIONAL ELECTRIC SAFETY CODE.
   (A)   Pursuant to C.R.S. Title 31, Art. 16, part 2, there is adopted by
reference the National Electric Safety Code, 1990 Edition, as published by the
Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers, Inc., 345 East 47th Street,
New York, NY 10017, subject to any amendments set forth herein, to protect the
public health, safety and welfare by providing minimum standards and
requirements pertaining to electrical installations.
   (B)   In case of any conflict between such code adopted herein and any other
specific provision of this municipal code, the specific provision of the
municipal code shall prevail.
(Prior Code, § 15.16.010) (Ord. 2017-2, passed 4-3-2017)
§ 150.05 UNIFORM PLUMBING CODE.
   (A)   Pursuant to C.R.S. Title 31, Art. 16, part 2, there is adopted by
reference the Uniform Plumbing Code, 1991 Edition, as published by the IAPMO
Publications Department, 20001 Walnut Drive South, Walnut, CA 91789-2825,
subject to any amendments set forth herein, to protect the public health,
safety and general welfare by providing minimum plumbing standards for new and
existing structures.
   (B)   In case of any conflict between such code adopted herein and any other
specific provision of this municipal code, the specific provision of the
municipal code shall prevail.
(Prior Code, § 15.16.010) (Ord. 2017-2, passed 4-3-2017)
§ 150.06 DANGEROUS BUILDING CODE.
   (A)   Pursuant to C.R.S. Title 31, Art. 16, part 2, there is adopted by
reference the Uniform Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings, 1991
Edition, as published by the International Conference of Building Officials,
5360 South Workman Mill Road, Whittier, CA 90601, subject to any amendments set
forth herein, to protect the public health, safety and welfare by providing a
just, equitable and practicable method, to be cumulative with and in addition
to any other remedy provided by the Building Code, Housing Code or otherwise
available by law, whereby buildings or structures that, from any cause,
endanger the life, limb, health, morals, property, safety or welfare of the
general public or their occupants, and providing a process by which the same
may be required to be repaired, vacated or demolished.
   (B)   In case of any conflict between such code adopted herein and any other
specific provision of this municipal code, the specific provision of the
municipal code shall prevail.
(Prior Code, § 15.20.010) (Ord. 2017-2, passed 4-3-2017)
BUILDING NUMBERING
§ 150.20 LOTS NUMBERED.
   All erections or other property abutting on any street or avenue shall be
numbered.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.010) (Ord. 167, passed - -1956)
§ 150.21 BASE LINES.
   Strohm Street shall constitute the base line for all numbering on the
streets running north or south, and Colorado Avenue shall constitute the base
line for all numbering on the streets running east and west.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.020) (Ord. 167, passed - -1956)
§ 150.22 NUMBERING.
   (A)   Erections fronting streets from the east and fronting streets from the
south shall bear even numbers in their last figure.
   (B)   Erections fronting streets from the west and from the north shall bear
odd numbers in their last figure.
   (C)   Erections fronting streets running north and south shall be numbered
from the base line, such numbers shall be 100 at the base line and not to
exceed the number 150 at the end of the first block either north or south of
the base line, 200 at the beginning and not to exceed the number 250 at the end
of the second block, either north or south of the base line. Such system shall
be in numbering all the streets running north and south in the town.
   (D)   Erections fronting streets running east and west shall be numbered
from the base line, such numbers shall be 100 at the base line and not to
exceed the number 150 at the end of the first block either east or west of the
base line, 200 at the beginning and not to exceed the number 250 at the end of
the second block either east or west of the base line. Such system shall be
followed in numbering all of the streets running east and west in the town.
   (E)   Where streets intersect, but do not cross, such intersection shall for
numbering purposes be deemed the end of the block for both sides of the street.
Where streets do not have an intersection on either side of the street, then
300 feet from the last intersection shall be deemed the end of a block for both
sides of the street.
   (F)   In each block, each 25 feet of frontage shall be given a number,
except where lots vary from 25 feet in width, such lots shall be numbered to
conform to the size of the lot. Fractions may be used if necessary to designate
a building located on a fractional part of a 25-foot frontage.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.030) (Ord. 167, passed - -1956)
§ 150.23 DESIGNATION OF STREETS.
   (A)   All lots or part of lots, houses and erections located on those
portions of any street extending north and south and being north of the Strohm
Street base line shall be known and designated as north and all south of the
Strohm Street base line shall be known and designated as south.
   (B)   All lots or parts of lots, houses and erections located on those
portions of any street extending east and west and being east of the Colorado
Avenue base line, shall be known and designated as east and all west of the
Colorado Avenue base line shall known and designated as west.
   (C)   The prefixes shall be placed before the proper name of the street as
West Strohm Street or North Colorado Avenue.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.040) (Ord. 167, passed - -1956)
§ 150.24 FIXING NUMBER.
   In case of doubt or where a question arises as to the proper number to be
assigned to any lot or building, the Town Clerk/Treasurer shall decide the
question and fix the number of such lot or building.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.050) (Ord. 167, passed - -1956)
§ 150.25 NUMBERS REQUIRED.
   On buildings now or hereafter erected and fronting on any street or alley
shall be conspicuously placed the number as provided by this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.060) (Ord. 167, passed - -1956)
§ 150.26 STYLE OF NUMBER.
   The number plate, placed upon any building shall be metal or wood, or the
number may be painted on the front of the building door, post, transom or other
place. The number shall be at least three inches in height and so as to be
easily seen from the street.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.070) (Ord. 167, passed - -1956)
§ 150.27 DUTY TO AFFIX NUMBER.
   (A)   It the owner or lessee of any building fails, refuses or neglects to
place the number, or replace it when necessary, the Town Clerk/Treasurer may
cause a notice to be personally served on the owner or lessee or mailed by
registered mail to his or her last known address, ordering him or her to place
or replace the number.
   (B)   The owner or lessee shall comply with the notice within ten days from
the date of service.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.080) (Ord. 167, passed - -1956)
FENCES, WALLS AND SIMILAR STRUCTURES
§ 150.40 FENCES, HEDGES AND WALLS ON RESIDENTIAL PROPERTIES.
   Fences, hedges and walls shall be allowed upon any residential property
within the town, subject to the following conditions and requirements.
   (A)   Walls or fences may be made of rock, brick and mortar constructed
under industry accepted standards of masonry. Fences may also be constructed of
ornamental iron, chain link, wood picket, solid wood and fence plastic, as
generally used in the geographical area. No other style or material may be used
without the written consent of the Town Superintendent, or designated officer
or agent of the town, including use of plywood, pressboard, waferboard,
chipboard, cardboard, aluminum, wood pallets, tarp material, black plastic or
similar materials or styles. Further, no fence shall be constructed of barbed
wire or sharp pointed materials, be electrically charged or be visibly
displeasing or objectionable to the general public.
      (1)   Temporary electrical fences surrounding garden areas in back
portions of private lots may be used, only during the growing months.
      (2)   Temporary fencing including the use of wood or plastic snow fence
for the purposes of limiting snow drifting between November 1 and April 1,
protection of excavation and construction sites, and the protection of plants
during grading and construction and during special events is permitted for up
to 60 consecutive days. Snow fences constructed of wood and wire and/or plastic
shall be permitted only as temporary fences.
   (B)   Hedges may be grown of any plant, bush or tree typically used as a
hedge; provided that, the hedge is trimmed and complies with all applicable
town ordinances.
   (C)   All fences, hedges and walls shall be subject to the applicable
sections of any ordinance of the code of the town.
   (D)   No fence, hedge or wall shall be placed upon town property, including
any easement used by or granted to the town, without the written consent of the
town through its designated officer or agent.
   (E)   It shall be the responsibility of the property owner to locate all
property lines prior to the placement of a fence, hedge or wall.
   (F)   Fences, hedges or walls shall not exceed four feet in height when such
fences are located within the front yard of the landowner’s property or within
25 feet of the town streets. Side and backyard fences shall not exceed eight
feet in height. In no event shall a fence, hedge or wall obstruct the vision of
automobile traffic on town streets, driveways or alleys, as determined by the
town. Fences may extend to 12 feet in height for tennis courts, or other
approved recreation purposes if a visual safety problem is not created by doing
so.
   (G)   Any such fence, hedge or wall which was constructed prior to the
adoption of this subchapter shall be allowed to remain where located unless the
town determines that the placement of the fence, hedge or wall constitutes a
safety problem, public nuisance, restricts the vision of automobile drivers and
bicyclists turning on a public street, turning into or out of an alley, is not
constructed of approved material, or the placement of the fence, hedge or wall
interferes with a town ordinance, policy or proper exercise of the town police
power. In such case, the town shall give written notice to the owner of the
fence, hedge or wall notifying the landowner to remove the fence, hedge or wall
for the reasons given, such notice to direct the fence, hedge or wall to be
removed within 30 days of the date of the notice.
   (H)   Any such fence, hedge or wall may not bock the natural flow of water
and have no restrictions to drainage or storm water on the property.
   (I)   All fences located around the back lots of properties must allow
access by gate to the town-owned electrical meters and all other town-owned
utilities. It is the property owner’s responsibility to replace and or repair
their fence if the town needs access to repair or replace any and all
utilities.
   (J)   Any and all fences, landscape walls or decorative posts shall be
erected so as to locate visible supports and other structural components toward
the subject property.
   (K)   Any and all fences, landscape walls or decorative posts shall be
maintained in a structurally sound and attractive manner as determined by the
Town Superintendent or designated officer or agent of the town.
(Ord. 2-2009, passed 9-2-2009) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.41 FENCES, HEDGES AND WALLS ON COMMERCIAL PROPERTIES.
   Fences, hedges and walls shall be allowed upon any commercial property
within the town, subject to the following conditions and requirements.
   (A)   All fences and walls may be constructed of the materials listed in §
150.40 of this chapter for residential property, along with the following
materials: security fencing topped by barbed wire, and strong barn (tin) may be
used. Galvanized fencing must be painted, no reflective metal may be used.
   (B)   All other regulations must be followed by commercial properties as
listed in §
150.40 of this chapter for residential properties.
(Ord. 2-2009, passed 9-2-2009) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.42 FENCE REQUIRED FOR SWIMMING POOLS.
   All properties with an outside swimming pool 24 inches deep or more must
install a fence with a self-locking gate around the pool area with the
following regulations:
   (A)   Any access gates through the enclosure open away from the swimming
pool and are self closing with a self-latching device placed no lower than 60
inches above the ground;
   (B)   A minimum fence height of 60 inches;
   (C)   A maximum vertical clearance from the ground to the bottom of the
enclosure of two inches;
   (D)   Gaps or voids, if any, do not allow passage of a sphere equal to or
greater than four inches in diameter; and
   (E)   An outside surface free of protrusions, cavities or other physical
characteristics that would serve as handholds or footholds that could enable a
child below the age of five years to climb over.
(Ord. 2-2009, passed 9-2-2009) Penalty, see §
150.99
§ 150.43 PERMIT REQUIRED FOR FENCES AND WALLS.
   Prior to the construction or replacement of a fence or wall, the landowner
shall apply for a building permit on a form provided by the Town Clerk/
Treasurer. The nature of the fence or wall to be constructed, the style and
material of the fence or wall is required. A sketch of the proposed fence
location is also required. The cost of the permit is set by resolution, and
sales and use tax on the building materials will also be collected by the Town
Clerk/Treasurer at the time of the permit application.
(Ord. 2-2009, passed 9-2-2009)
§ 150.44 ABATEMENT.
   Should any fence, hedge or wall be constructed, maintained, replaced or
planted within the town, either without the landowner first obtaining a permit
for a fence or wall and/or the fence, hedge or wall being in violation of the
provisions of this subchapter. The town may provide written notice to the
landowner requiring that the landowner take action to cease and desist
construction of the fence or wall, or that the landowner’s property be brought
into compliance with town ordinances within a reasonable time, such time not to
exceed 30 days from the date of the notice. If the landowner fails or refuses
to bring the offending property into compliance, the town may seek enforcement
through a citation to the Municipal Court. Remedies available to the town shall
include the right to bring the offending property into compliance and to access
the costs, including the town’s reasonable attorney fees, incurred in the
enforcement of this subchapter, to the offending property.
(Ord. 2-2009, passed 9-2-2009)
§ 150.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Anyone violating any of the provisions of §§
150.20 through
150.27 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be subject to a fine not
exceeding $25.
(Prior Code, § 12.20.090)
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to maintain
any property of cause or permit the same to be done in violation of the terms
of §§
150.40 through
150.44 of this chapter. Those persons or entities in violation of the
provisions of §§
150.40 through
150.44 of this chapter may be subject to a fine not to exceed $500 for each
violation of §§
150.40 through
150.44 of this chapter, for each day that the property is not in compliance
with the provisions of §§
150.40 through
150.44 of this chapter.
(Ord. 167, passed - -1956; Ord. 2-2009, passed 9-2-2009)
CHAPTER 151: HOUSING CODE
Section
   
151.01   Definition
   
151.02   Restrictions
   
151.03   Non-conforming structures
 
   
151.99   Penalty
§ 151.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   MANUFACTURED HOME means a structure built in one, two or more sections that
is partially or entirely fabricated, formed or assembled at a location other
than the site of the completed home, that is designed for residential occupancy
in either a temporary or permanent location, that does not have motive power
and that is not licensed as a recreational vehicle.
(Ord. 2019-2, passed 2-4-2019)
§ 151.02 RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   Building permits must be obtained prior to the construction, moving or
alteration of any manufactured home in accordance with Chapter 150 of this code
of ordinances.
   (B)   No manufactured home shall be introduced into or placed within the
town, which is manufactured earlier than five years prior to its introduction
or placement into the town.
   (C)   A manufactured home must be set on excavated, backfilled, engineered
foundation enclosed at the perimeter. Such foundation shall meet or exceed the
standards established by the state for the placement of manufactured homes.
   (D)   The foundation for manufactured homes shall be similar in appearance
and durability to a masonry foundation of a site-built dwelling. The foundation
shall provide an anchoring system for the manufactured home that is totally
concealed under the structure.
   (E)   The manufactured home must have brick, wood or cosmetically equivalent
exterior siding on all exterior walls which provides a constant, continuous
facade from the bottom of the soffit (top of the wall section) downward to the
top of the exposed perimeter foundation. The exterior siding of the
manufactured home must have the same appearance as materials commonly used on
residential dwellings. Metal siding must be painted or anodized.
   (F)   The manufactured home must have a pitched roof with a pitch of at
least nominal three/twelve (3:12). The roof must be covered with shingles,
shakes or tile. A non-galvanized, colored metal roof may be used instead of
shingles. Eves of roof must extend at least one foot from the inner section of
the roof and the exterior walls.
   (G)   The manufactured home must have windows that are wood, vinyl coated or
anodized. The manufactured home must have color coordinated body and trim.
Colors of both the factory components and the site-built components shall be
the same.
   (H)   The main entrance of the manufactured home must face or be oriented
toward the street as the lot allows. As used in this section, STREET shall mean
the street of the home’s address. Mobile homes located in a mobile home park
are exempt from this requirement.
   (I)   The manufactured home shall be sited on the lot so that the placement
is consistent and compatible with the placement of other residential units in
the surrounding neighborhood.
   (J)   The transportation mechanisms, including the wheels, axles and hitch
must be removed from the manufactured home.
   (K)   All manufactured homes shall be certified pursuant to the
aforementioned National Manufactured Housing Construction and Safety Standards
Act of 1974, 42 U.S.C. §§ 5401 et seq., as amended.
   (L)   The manufactured home must meet or exceed all equivalent performance-
engineering standards to the same extent required for other single-family
housing units.
   (M)   All manufactured homes shall be inspected by the town’s Building
Inspector prior to issuance of a certificate of occupancy by the town.
(Ord. 2019-2, passed 2-4-2019) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.03 NON-CONFORMING STRUCTURES.
   Any manufactured home existing in the town upon the date of this chapter,
which does not conform to the specifications and requirements of this chapter
may not be moved from one location in the town to another and may not be
modified, enlarged or altered, except in a manner conforming to the
requirements of this chapter.
(Ord. 2019-2, passed 2-4-2019) Penalty, see §
151.99
§ 151.99 PENALTY.
   Any person who violates this chapter, upon conviction thereof, shall be
punished by a fine not to exceed $300. Each day of a continuing violation shall
be deemed a separate violation. It shall be the duty of the town’s Building
Inspector to enforce the provisions of this chapter and to bring to the
attention of the proper enforcement officers of the town any violations
thereof, and when required for the proper enforcement of this chapter, it shall
be the duty of the town’s Building Inspector to make and file with the Police
Department a written complaint against any such violator.
(Ord. 2019-2, passed 2-4-2019)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 152.01 PLAYING IN STREETS.
   No person or persons shall roll any hoop, play ball, fly a kite or engage in
any other game or amusement tending to annoy any person near thereto, while in
or upon any street or alley or other public place within the town.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.010) (Ord. 35, passed - -1911) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.02 THROWING TRASH ONTO STREETS.
   No person shall place, throw, dump or leave within the town, any fuel,
ashes, paper, glass, cans, boxing or refuse of any sort or kind in any street
or alley or in any place where the same can be carried by the wind into any
street or alley, nor shall any person place, dump or throw any fuel or ashes in
any place other than a pit or enclosure where the contents are protected from
the wind.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.020) (Ord. 35, passed - -1911) Penalty, see §
152.99

   Nuisances, see §§

   Solid waste, see

   Trash as a fire hazard, see §

§ 152.03 CLEANING AND SNOW REMOVAL.
   (A)   Snow removal on sidewalks by owner required. All persons, companies,
corporations owning or occupying premises in the town shall be required to
hereafter keep the sidewalks in front of and adjacent to the tenements or
grounds owned and occupied by them in the town, free and clear of ice, mud,
dirt and rubbish and filth, and after any fall of snow or accumulation of ice,
shall cause the snow or accumulation of ice to be removed from the sidewalk
with 12 hours from and after the snow has ceased to fall, and if they fail to
remove the accumulation of snow or ice within the time prescribed, the town, by
its duly authorized officers may, without further notice, remove the same at
the expense of the property owner or occupant, and such failure on the part of
the owner or occupant shall be deemed a violation of this section, and may be
punished as provided in this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 12.08.010)
   (B)   Removal of weeds, rubbish and dirt required. All persons, firms or
corporations are required to keep the streets in front of the tenements or
grounds or lots occupied or owned by them free and clear of weeds, to the
center of the highway, and to keep all premises owned by them free and clear of
rubbish, dirt and filth.
(Prior Code, § 12.08.020)
   (C)   Removal by tenants nearest sidewalks.
      (1)   Where houses and other buildings are occupied by several tenants,
it shall be the duty of the person or persons occupying the tenements, store or
stores nearest the sidewalks, gutters, ditches or streets, as well as the
owners of the property to comply with the requirements of divisions (A) and (B)
above.
      (2)   Where the basement of any house or other building reaches below the
level of the ground, for the purpose of this section, the second story shall be
deemed the nearest as aforesaid, and the basement or first story, the nearest
after the second story; provided that, no such tenant shall be required to keep
clear as aforesaid any such sidewalks or streets for a greater number of feet
than may be contiguous or opposite to any premises or any part of premises
occupied by him or her.
(Prior Code, § 12.08.030)
   (D)   Removal by owner if unoccupied. Where any premises or parts of
premises are not occupied in any manner as aforesaid, it shall be the duty of
the owner thereof to comply with the requirements of divisions (A) through (C)
above, so far as no other provisions are made.
(Prior Code, § 12.08.040)
   (E)   Removal by agent if owner non-resident. In the event the owner of any
premises so unoccupied is a non-resident of the town and absent from the town,
any responsible agent shall comply with the requirements of this section, and
any notice served upon the agent shall be notice to the property owner.
(Prior Code, § 12.08.050)
(Ord. 60, passed - -1918) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.04 HEAVY VEHICLES AND MACHINERY.
   It shall be the duty of all persons, associations and corporations operating
or moving steam threshing machines, steam engines, tractors or other heavy
vehicles or other heavy machinery of whatever character over or along the
streets of the town, and over the crossings, crosswalks, bridges, culverts or
causeways within the town, to use a sufficient number of heavy planks whenever
necessary to protect such sidewalks, crossings, crosswalks, bridges, culverts
or causeways from being in any manner broken or in any way injured by the
transportation of the vehicles over and across the same; and no vehicles
abovementioned or heavy-loaded wagons shall be driven across walks at any other
place, except at regular crossing.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.010) (Ord. 57, passed - -1917) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.05 CURBLINES AND TREE SETBACKS.
   (A)   Curbs.
      (1)   Specifications.
         (a)   All curbs hereafter constructed throughout the town shall be
constructed at established grades and at certain uniform distances from
property lines, such distances to be for the several streets and avenues
throughout the town as follows:
            1.   On Colorado Avenue north of Chase Street, 15 feet from
property line;
            2.   On Colorado Avenue, south of Chase Street, 12 feet from
property line; and
            3.   On all streets which are 80 feet between property lines, curbs
shall be constructed 25 feet from property line.
         (b)   On all streets which are sixty feet from property line, the curb
shall be constructed fifteen feet from the property line, with the following
exceptions:
            1.   On Fletcher Street, between Logan and Washington Avenues,
curbs shall constructed ten feet from the property line;
            2.   On Logan and Washington Avenues, where curbs shall be
constructed ten feet from property line;
            3.   On Strohm Street between Logan and Washington Avenues, where
curbs shall be constructed ten feet from property line; and
            4.   On Logan Avenue from the north side of the right-of-way of the
Burlington Northern Railroad to the north line of the town, where curbs shall
be constructed 15 feet from the property line.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.010)
      (2)   Reconstruction according to lines established herein. Any person
who hereafter builds or constructs any curb on any street or avenue in the town
at a distance from a property line contrary to the provisions of this section
applying to such street or avenue may be required by resolution of the Board of
Trustees at any regular or special meeting, to tear out such curb and
reconstruct same at the line as is laid down in this section.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.020)
   (B)   Trees.
      (1)   Specifications. All shade and ornamental trees hereafter planted or
set out by property owners within the town shall be planted or set ten feet
from property lines.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.030)
      (2)   Any further planting to comply. Any person who shall hereafter
plant or set out any trees along streets or avenues in the town, contrary to
specifications of this section, may be required by resolution of the Board of
Trustees at any regular meeting to remove the trees to the required distance
from the property line.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.040)
   (C)   Not applicable to curbs or trees already in place; exceptions. This
section shall not affect the location of any shade or ornamental trees or the
location of any curb already constructed within the town unless it appears to
the Board of Trustees that such trees or such curbs are placed so as to cause
interference with adjoining property owners or so as to seriously mar the
appearance of any such street or avenue and in such event any person may make
complaint to the Board of Trustees and the Board of Trustees may, upon hearing
such complaint and reply thereto, order the shade or ornamental trees or curb
to be moved or to be torn out and rebuilt at the proper distance from the
property line as laid down in this section.
(Prior Code, § 12.16.050)
(Ord. 76, passed - -; Ord. 109, passed - -; Ord. 118, passed - -1934) Penalty,
see §
152.99
Cross-reference:
   Trees generally, see
Ch. 153.
§ 152.06 CONCRETE CROSSINGS.
   (A)   Generally. All concrete crossings to be constructed in the future
shall be composed, laid and built in accordance with the specifications and
rules set out in this section.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.010)
   (B)   Composition. The crossing shall be composed of five parts clean creek
gravel of a size to pass through a one-inch screen and one part of best
portland cement or of a cement of equal grade.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.020)
   (C)   Mixture.
      (1)   Wet. The gravel and cement shall be mixed in a machine with water
enough to form what is known as a wet mixture wet enough to run off a shovel,
but not wet enough to form a slop.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.030)
      (2)   Uniformity. The crossings shall be of the same kind of mixture
throughout with no surface of a finer mixture.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.040)
   (D)   Width. The crossing shall be not less than four feet in width on the
top and there shall be a six-inch slope on each side in addition, making five
feet over all.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.050)
   (E)   Depth. The crossings shall not be less than six inches in depth at all
points, including the sloping shoulders which shall be made full depth and not
feathered to an edge.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.060)
   (F)   Conformity with crown. The crossings shall conform to the construction
of the street so as to have the same crown as shall be provided for the street
by survey of same.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.070)
   (G)   Tamping. The crossings shall be well tamped down by hand so as to be a
compact mass of concrete.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.080)
   (H)   With gutter or drain. In the event the Board of Trustees orders any
crossings to be built with a gutter or drain, then such crossings shall conform
to the specifications of this section and, in addition, be provided with a
gutter beneath same constructed in accordance with specifications to be
furnished by the Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.090)
   (I)   Supervision. It shall be the duty of the Street Commissioner to
supervise the laying of all concrete crossings and to pass upon same and no
such crossing shall be paid for by the Board of Trustees until such
Commissioner reports to the Board of Trustees that the crossing was laid in all
respects in accordance with this section.
(Prior Code, § 12.28.100)
(Ord. 73, passed - -1920) Penalty, see §
152.99
SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION
§ 152.20 SPECIFICATIONS GENERALLY.
   (A)   All sidewalks on Colorado Avenue or Main Street, between the center of
the Burlington Northern Railroad right-of-way and Strohm Street on Colorado
Avenue, and all sidewalks on Fletcher Street and Raymond Street, between Logan
Street and Washington Street, at right angles with Colorado Avenue, shall be
eight feet in width.
   (B)   All sidewalks on Strohm Street from Logan to Washington shall be six
feet in width and shall be so constructed that the outer edge of the walk shall
be on the lot line of the front line of the lot along which the sidewalk is
constructed.
   (C)   (1)   All other sidewalks within the town shall be of a width of four
feet, and shall be so constructed that the outer edge of the walk shall be two
feet from the front line of their lot along which the sidewalk is constructed,
except in such certain blocks of the town exclusive of Colorado Avenue where
sidewalks have already been constructed prior to the date of the passage of the
ordinance codified in this subchapter, at a different distance from the front
line of the lot and on said blocks only.
      (2)   The distance from the front line of the lot shall correspond to the
walks already constructed.
   (D)   All walks shall be constructed upon the grade line of the street as
established by ordinances with an even slope toward the gutter or curbstone of
0.12 of one foot to keep the sidewalk free from water, the grade for the
sidewalk to be furnished by the Street Commissioner or the Board of Trustees on
application therefor.
   (E)   All sidewalks shall be constructed in the same manner, and on streets
where the grade is not established by ordinance.
   (F)   They shall be constructed on a uniform grade to be furnished by and
under the supervision of the Street Commissioner or Board of Trustees.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.010) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
Cross-reference:
   Building and construction, see
Ch. 150.
§ 152.21 REPAIR OR REBUILDING SPECIFICATIONS.
   (A)   All sidewalks within the town, as now defined or hereafter extended by
ordinance, shall be constructed, widened, repaired or rebuilt with cement or
brick only, and such sidewalks, widened, repaired or rebuilt upon Main Street
or Colorado Avenue within the fire limits of the town shall be built, widened,
repaired or rebuilt with a curbing on the outside of the cement, not less than
five inches in thickness and not less than 16 inches wide nor less than four
feet long.
   (B)   Sidewalks outside of the fire limits and the others within, not
covered by the above, shall be constructed, widened, repaired, or rebuilt,
shall, if constructed of cement, be constructed, widened, repaired or rebuilt
as set out in §§
152.22 through
152.27 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.020) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.22 EXCAVATION SPECIFICATIONS.
   The ground on the side of the walk shall be excavated not less than seven
inches below the grade line for a walk four feet wide and narrower, and not
less than nine inches below the grade line for a walk wider than four feet.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.030) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.23 FILLING SPECIFICATIONS.
   The excavation shall be filled for four inches below grade line, with a
filling of sand and gravel well-packed.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.040) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.24 CONCRETE BOTTOM SPECIFICATIONS.
   The concrete bottom where cement is used shall be composed of six parts sand
and gravel to one part portland cement or other cement of equal grade, and laid
on the filling mentioned in §
152.23 of this chapter, and packed three-fourths of an inch below the grade
line.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.050) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.25 TOP SPECIFICATIONS.
   (A)   The top shall be composed of two parts sand screened not finer than
number five and one part of portland cement or other cement of equal grade, and
spread not less than three-fourths of an inch thick on the concrete bottom
immediately after being laid and packed in place.
   (B)   The top coat shall be struck to a true plane with a straight edge, or
troweled smooth, or both.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.060) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.26 JOINTS SPECIFICATIONS.
   (A)   Cement walks four feet wide shall have expansion joints not farther
than five feet apart.
   (B)   Cement walks six or eight feet wide shall have expansion joints
cutting the walk into blocks not larger than five feet by five feet.
   (C)   No walk shall be cut into blocks larger than 30 square feet.
   (D)   Joint space to be not less than one-fourth of an inch clear through.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.070) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.27 CURB SPECIFICATIONS.
   All concrete walks wider than four feet shall have a curb six inches thick,
and extend below the grade line 12 inches, or deeper if necessary, to reach
virgin soil. The curb is to be of the same material as the walk.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.080) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.28 RESOLUTION REQUIRING TWO-INCH EXPANSION JOINT.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees of the town in regular session adopted a
resolution requiring at least a two-inch expansion joint between any cement
work and the curb; this joint to be filled with asphalt to protect curbing from
breaking from expansion.
   (B)   This resolution is in effect after the first publication and applies
to all cement work within the town limits.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.090) (Res. passed 3-6-1939)
§ 152.29 CONSTRUCTING OBSTRUCTIONS; REPAIRING UNDER SUPERVISION, ORDER OF TOWN
OFFICIALS.
   No scale stands, hitch racks, hitching posts or other obstruction shall
hereafter be erected, kept or maintained in front of any sidewalk provided in
this subchapter to be six or eight feet in width, and no walks shall be
constructed, widened, repaired or rebuilt in the town, without notice to and
under the supervision of the Board of Trustees or Street Commissioner who shall
be by the owner notified thereof and in case the same is not provided for by
ordinance, shall designate the width and grade, and how the same shall be
constructed, as provided in this subchapter, and in cases where a sidewalk has
been broken, worn or defective, it shall be the duty of the Commissioner to
notify the owner, agent or person having charge of the property adjoining the
sidewalk needing repair and to order the necessary repairs made thereon within
a reasonable time, which shall be stated in the notice, and any person so
notified shall repair the walk within the time stated in this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.100) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917) Penalty, see §
152.99
§ 152.30 OWNER RESPONSIBILITY; TOWN RESPONSIBILITY.
   All sidewalks in the town and the necessary grading for the same shall be
constructed, widened, repaired and when necessary rebuilt, by the owners of the
property fronting or abutting on the same, at the expense of the owner and the
necessary grading for sidewalks shall be deemed and included as a part of the
construction of the sidewalks.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.110) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.31 ADOPTION OF ORDINANCE REQUIRING SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION.
   Whenever it appears to the Board of Trustees by petition or otherwise that a
sidewalk should be constructed, widened, repaired or rebuilt within the town,
it may, by ordinance, order the construction, widening, repairing or
reconstruction, or the same by the owner of the property fronting on the same
and at the owner’s expense; provided that, the concurrence of at least four of
the members elected to the Board of Trustees shall be necessary to adopt such
ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.120) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.32 NOTICE TO REPAIR/CONSTRUCT; PERIOD OF TIME.
   (A)   Whenever the Board of Trustees directs or orders the construction,
widening, repairing or reconstruction of any sidewalk by ordinance as
aforesaid, it shall state therein the period of time within which the owner may
have to construct, widen, repair or reconstruct such sidewalk, which period
shall be not less than ten days, nor more than 20 days from the date of the
passage of the ordinance codified in this subchapter, and the Town Clerk/
Treasurer shall immediately notify all owners of property fronting on the same,
their agents or persons occupying or having charge of such property, in
writing, of such order, stating therein the period of time within which the
owner may have to construct, widen, repair or reconstruct the sidewalk.
   (B)   If the owner, agent or person having charge is absent or unknown, the
notice may be served by posting the same in a conspicuous place on such lot or
premises, and mailing a copy of the notice, properly stamped and addressed, to
the owner at his or her present post office address, and the posting of the
notice and mailing a copy as stated shall be deemed and held to be a complete
service of the same.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.130) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.33 FAILURE TO REPAIR/CONSTRUCT; ASSESSMENT TO PROPERTY OWNER FOR WORK
DONE BY TOWN; LIEN.
   If the property owners shall not construct, widen, repair or reconstruct the
sidewalks or other improvements, according to the requirements of such
ordinance within the time therein named after service of such notice upon them,
the Board of Trustees may order that such sidewalk be constructed, widened,
repaired or reconstructed by or under the direction of the Street Commissioner
and assess the cost thereof against the property fronting upon the sidewalk,
and the amount so assessed shall be the cost of construction, widening,
repairing or reconstruction of the sidewalk, and shall include the cost of the
service and publication of notice, and all expenses made necessary by these
proceedings and the amount so assessed shall be a lien upon the property until
the same is paid.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.140) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.34 STATEMENT OF COST ACCEPTANCE; NOTICE OF ASSESSMENT; HEARING;
COLLECTION AS TAXES.
   (A)   The statement of the Street Commissioner or the Board of Trustees of
the cost and expense of the sidewalk as apportioned by the Board of Trustees,
or by him or her, under its direction shall be accepted as correct and, if such
assessment is not paid within ten days after making the same, the Town Clerk/
Treasurer shall cause a notice of such assessment to be given to the owners,
and all other persons interested in such property as can reasonably be
ascertained, by publication in a newspaper, published in the town for two
successive weeks being two publications only, and the notice shall state the
amount assessed against each lot or other subdivision of property, and
designate a time and place, not less than 30 days after the first publication,
when the Board of Trustees will hear any objections.
   (B)   The owner and other persons interested in the property shall make, and
the Board of Trustees may correct and perfect any such assessment improperly or
incorrectly made. The Town Clerk/Treasurer shall certify the assessment to the
Assessor of the county, or other proper assessing officer then having
possession of the tax list, to be by him or her placed on the tax list for the
current year, and to be collected in the same manner as other taxes are
collected, with a 10% penalty thereon to defray the cost of collection.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.150) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.35 SUIT FOR COLLECTION.
   If the Board of Trustees so elects, it may bring suit in any court of
competent jurisdiction to enforce the lien and collect the assessment.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.160) (Ord. 50, passed - -1917)
§ 152.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Any person violating the provisions of §
152.01 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined any sum not exceeding
$10 and costs of conviction, to be enforced and collected in the manner
provided by law therefor.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.010)
   (C)   Any violation of §
152.02 of this chapter shall subject the offender to a fine of not more than
$25 and costs of conviction, to be enforced and collected in the manner
provided by law therefor.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.020)
   (D)   Any person, firm or corporation who fails to comply with any of the
provisions of §
152.03 of this chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, be fined in a sum not less than $1, nor more than $25, and
costs of suit; and, provided further that, the town may cause all the aforesaid
work or duties to be done by the duly authorized person or persons acting for
the town, and the expense thereof shall be charged up to and assessed and taxed
against the property or properties of the persons who fail to comply with the
provisions aforesaid, the sum or any sums thus expended may be recovered
against the owner or occupant of the property, convicted of a violation of §
152.03 of this chapter in a civil action brought for that purpose.
(Prior Code, § 12.08.060)
   (E)   (1)   If any person, association or corporation destroys or injures
any sidewalk, crosswalk, bridge, culvert or causeway within the town, by the
transportation over the same of any of the heavy machinery or vehicles as set
out in §
152.04 of this chapter, or in any way or manner violates §
152.04 of this chapter, he or she shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, shall be fined in a sum of not less than $5, nor more than $100,
and costs of suit and shall also be liable for all damages occasioned thereby,
and for the necessary cost of rebuilding and repairing the sidewalk, crosswalk,
bridge, culvert or causeway so injured.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.020)
      (2)   It is further provided that the penalty and damages provided for by
§
152.04 of this chapter may be, at the option of the Board of Trustees,
recovered in a civil action brought in a court of record in the county for that
purpose.
(Prior Code, § 12.12.030)
   (F)   Any person or persons who fail to make such walk or repairs after
notice, per §
152.29 of this chapter, or shall be guilty of a violation of any of the
provisions of §§
152.20 through
152.35 of this chapter shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in a sum not
less than $50 and costs of suit.
(Prior Code, § 12.24.100)
(Ord. 35, passed - -1911; Ord. 50, passed - -1917; Ord. 57, passed - -1917;
Ord. 60, passed - -1918)
CHAPTER 153: TREES
Section
   
153.01   Maintenance of trees and shrubs
   
153.02   Removal of dead or dangerous trees and roots
   
153.03   Control of disease or insect infestation
   
153.04   Compliance with notices
   
153.05   Delivery of notice
   
153.06   Failure of property owner to do required work
   
153.07   Assessment of delinquent costs
   
153.08   Administration
   
153.09   Right of entry
 
   
153.99   Penalty
§ 153.01 MAINTENANCE OF TREES AND SHRUBS.
   (A)   (1)   It shall be the duty of the owner of property abutting the
right-of-way of any street, alley and sidewalk or other public place to
maintain and care for all trees and shrubs on such property owner to perform
such maintenance on any tree or shrub of the right-of-way abutting such owner’s
property as may be necessary.
      (2)   The town shall further have the power to require any property owner
to trim, remove or protect any tree or shrub on such owner’s property which may
project beyond the property line onto or over the right-of-way abutting the
same.
      (3)   Trees and shrubs must not obstruct the clear view at any
intersection. A CLEAR VIEW is defined as 150 feet in both directions of the
intersecting road from a point of ten feet from the beginning of the
intersection.
      (4)   The town shall cause a notice requiring such work be done within
the reasonable time specified in this notice.
   (B)   Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as requiring the owner of
property to trim any trees or shrubs when such trimming is required on public
ways because of town utility lines, traffic-control signs or devices, and it
shall be the duty of the town to do any trimming on public ways as required for
such utilities or signs or traffic-control devices.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.010) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.02 REMOVAL OF DEAD OR DANGEROUS TREES AND ROOTS.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of the owner of any property abutting the right-
of-way of any street, alley, sidewalk or other public place to remove any dead
or dying trees or limbs or roots that are heaving sidewalks that are dangerous
to life, limb or property located upon the premises of such owner or upon the
right-of-way of any street, alley, sidewalk or other public place abutting the
property of such owner of property.
   (B)   The town shall give notice to the property owner for such removal when
required. All newly cut trees shall be removed from city limits for a period of
18 months.
   (C)   No wood shall be brought into the city limits that has been cut less
than 18 months. Such work specified in such notice.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.020) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.03 CONTROL OF DISEASE OR INSECT INFESTATION.
   Upon the discovery of any destructive or communicable disease or other
pestilence which endangers the growth, health, life or well-being of trees or
plants, or wood piles in the town, or which is capable of causing an epidemic
spread of communicable disease or insect infestation such as Dutch Elm Disease,
the town shall, at once, cause written notice to be served upon the owner of
the property abutting the right-of-way of any street, alley, sidewalk or other
public place upon which such diseased tree is situated, which notice shall
require such property owner to eradicate, remove or otherwise control such
condition within a reasonable time to be specified in such notice.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.030) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989)
§ 153.04 COMPLIANCE WITH NOTICES.
   It is unlawful for any person to fail to comply with the requirements of any
notice given pursuant to this chapter within the time specified in such notice.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.040) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989) Penalty, see §
153.99
§ 153.05 DELIVERY OF NOTICE.
   (A)   Any notice may be served by delivering a copy of such notice to the
record owner of such property or be leaving a copy of such notice at such
owner’s usual place of abode with some member of his or her family over the age
of 18 years.
   (B)   In case there is more than one owner of a property, service upon any
owner shall be adequate service upon all co-owners.
   (C)   If the owner of any property cannot be found in the town, service may
be made by mailing a copy thereof to his or her last known address, and by
posting a copy of such notice in a conspicuous place on the premises involved.
   (D)   Service by mail shall be completed five days after the date the notice
is deposited in the mail and posted on the premises.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.050) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989)
§ 153.06 FAILURE OF PROPERTY OWNER TO DO REQUIRED WORK.
   (A)   If any work required is not accomplished within the time specified in
the notice, the town shall cause the work to be done and the cost of the same
shall be collected from the property owner.
   (B)   Any notice given pursuant to this chapter shall state that if the work
required is not done within the time specified, the town will cause the same to
be done at the expense of the property owner.
   (C)   If the town causes the work to be done, it shall submit the cost
thereof to the Town Clerk/Treasurer who shall send a statement in such amount
to the property owner at his or her last known address.
   (D)   Any such statement shall be paid by the property owner within 30 days
and any unpaid amount shall bear interest at the legal rate.
   (E)   If any property owner is unable to pay the cost of such work within 30
days, he or she may enter into an agreement for the payment of the same monthly
installments over a period not to exceed five years; and the unpaid cost shall,
by such agreement, be made a lien to the lands of such property owner.
   (F)   Any unpaid balance due under such agreement shall bear interest at the
legal rate.
   (G)   The agreement shall be filed in the office of the County Clerk and
County Recorder.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.060) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989)
§ 153.07 ASSESSMENT OF DELINQUENT COSTS.
   (A)   The Town Clerk/Treasurer shall not later than July 1 each year, report
to the Board of Trustees as to any costs for work done by the town under this
chapter which have now been paid by the property owner or made the subject of
an agreement with the property owner as authorized.
   (B)   Notice shall be mailed by the Town Clerk/Treasurer to each property
owner, which notice shall state the amount claimed to be due from such property
owner, the date, place and time that the report will be made to the Board of
Trustees, the description of the property to be assessed, a description of the
work performed, and that the Board of Trustees will be asked to assess the cost
of work, together with an amount to cover interest, advertising fees and cost
of collection against the property of such owner.
   (C)   Such notice shall be mailed at least ten days, and not more than 45
days, before the date the report will be made to the Board of Trustees. Such
assessment shall be certified by the Town Clerk/Treasurer to the County
Treasurer and shall be on a parity with the tax lien for general state, county,
city, town or school taxes.
   (D)   Such assessment shall become delinquent on September 1, after the same
time or times, in the same manner and under all the same conditions and
penalties and with the same effect as prescribed by the general laws of the
state for the sale of real estate in default of payment of general taxes.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.070) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989)
§ 153.08 ADMINISTRATION.
   This chapter shall be administered and enforced by the superintendent of the
town or such person as the Board of Trustees appoints and shall also be known
as town’s “Tree Ordinance Enforcement Officer”.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.080) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989)
§ 153.09 RIGHT OF ENTRY.
   In order to accomplish the purpose of this chapter, the town’s designated
official is authorized to go upon any property in the town for the purpose of
inspecting trees, shrubs and other plants.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.090) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989)
§ 153.99 PENALTY.
   Violation under this chapter will be punishable by fine, pursuant to this
municipal code.
(Prior Code, § 12.32.100) (Ord. 89-2, passed - -1989; Ord. 2020-2, passed 5-4-
2020)
CHAPTER 154: AIRPORT
Section
   
154.01   Power to acquire
   
154.02   Maintenance; fees
   
154.03   Rules and regulations
   
154.04   Airport Manager; duties; salary
   
154.05   Aircraft and pilot certification
   
154.06   Compliance with federal regulations required
   
154.07   Careless or reckless operation prohibited
 
   
154.99   Penalty
§ 154.01 POWER TO ACQUIRE.
   The Board of Trustees shall have the power to acquire to purchase or
otherwise acquire, establish, construct, own, control, lease, equip, improve,
maintain and operate an airport and landing field for the use of airplanes and
other aircraft without the town limits.
(Prior Code, § 13.16.010) (Ord. 193, passed - -1964)
§ 154.02 MAINTENANCE; FEES.
   (A)   The Haxtun Airport shall be maintained, operated and controlled by the
Board of Trustees or by an Airport Committee appointed by the Board of
Trustees.
   (B)   The Board of Trustees shall from time to time, by resolution,
establish uniform schedule of fees to be charged for the use of the airport.
(Prior Code, § 13.16.020) (Ord. 193, passed - -1964)
§ 154.03 RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   The Board of Trustees shall adopt rules and regulations governing the use
and operation of the Haxtun Airport and any violation of such rules and
regulations shall constitute a violation of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 13.16.030) (Ord. 193, passed - -1964)
§ 154.04 AIRPORT MANAGER; DUTIES; SALARY.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees may employ an Airport Manager or Superintendent,
who shall, subject to the direction and control of the Board of Trustees,
manage and control the operation and maintenance of the airport, and enforce
the ordinances, rules and regulations pertaining thereto.
   (B)   The Board of Trustees may pay a salary to the Airport Manager or it
may provide for his or her compensation by allowing him or her to retain
certain designated airport fees as salary.
   (C)   The Board of Trustees may employ such other personnel as it deems
necessary or desirable for the operation of the airport.
(Prior Code, § 13.16.040) (Ord. 193, passed - -1964)
§ 154.05 AIRCRAFT AND PILOT CERTIFICATION.
   It is unlawful for any person to operate any aircraft within or over the
corporate limits of the city or into or from the Haxtun Airport unless such
person holds a currently valid airman certificate issued by the Federal
Aviation Administration and unless such aircraft carries therein a currently
effective aircraft registration certificate issued by the Federal Aviation
Administrator and a currently effective certificate of airworthiness issued by
the Federal Aviation Administration.
(Prior Code, § 13.16.050) (Ord. 193, passed - -1964) Penalty, see §
154.99
§ 154.06 COMPLIANCE WITH FEDERAL REGULATIONS REQUIRED.
   It is unlawful for any person to operate any aircraft within or over the
town or into or from the Haxtun Airport in violation of any rule or regulation
of the Federal Aviation Administration, including those relating to air
traffic, lights and other safety devices and equipment, or minimum altitude of
flight.
(Prior Code, § 13.16.060) (Ord. 193, passed - -1964) Penalty, see §
154.99
§ 154.07 CARELESS OR RECKLESS OPERATION PROHIBITED.
   It is unlawful for any person to operate any aircraft over the corporate
limits of the town or over the Haxtun Airport in a careless or reckless manner
so as to endanger life or property.
(Prior Code, § 13.16.070) (Ord. 193, passed - -1964) Penalty, see §
154.99
§ 154.99 PENALTY.
   Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of this chapter,
upon conviction thereof, shall be fined not less than $25, nor more than $100,
for each offense.
(Prior Code, § 13.16.010) (Ord. 193, passed - -1964)
CHAPTER 155: RESIDENTIAL SOLAR SYSTEMS
Section
   
155.01   Definitions
   
155.02   Eligibility
   
155.03   Request
   
155.04   System effects
   
155.05   System upgrades
   
155.06   Agreements
   
155.07   Codes and permits
   
155.08   Certificate of completion
   
155.09   Normal operation
   
155.10   Character of service
   
155.11   Code requirements
   
155.12   Generating facility control and operation
   
155.13   Fault current contribution
   
155.14   Reclosing coordination
   
155.15   Disconnect device
   
155.16   Standards for interconnection, safety and operating reliability
§ 155.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   CUSTOMER. Any entity interconnected to the town’s distribution system for
the purpose of receiving retail electric power service from town’s distribution
system.
   DISTRIBUTION SYSTEM. The town’s facilities and equipment used to transmit
electricity to ultimate usage points, such as homes and industries directly
from nearby generators or from interchanges with higher voltage transmission
networks which transport bulk power over longer distances and from town’s
wholesale supplier.
   ELECTRIC WHOLESALE SUPPLIER or EWS. The town’s total requirements electric
wholesale supplier.
   FACILITIES INTERCONNECTION AGREEMENT or CUSTOMER-OWNED GENERATION FACILITIES
INTERCONNECTION AGREEMENT. The meaning set forth in §
155.06 of this chapter.
   GENERATING FACILITY. The customer’s device for the conversion of renewable
generation of solar energy to electricity, as identified in the interconnection
application and able to be certified as a qualifying facility under the
definitions of the Public Utility Regulatory Policies Act (PURPA, Pub. Law No.
95-617, 92 Stat. 3117, enacted 11-9-1978), a United States act passed as part
of the National Energy Act, and as amended.
   GOOD UTILITY PRACTICE. Any of the practices, methods and acts engaged in or
approved by a significant portion of the electric industry during the relevant
time period, or any of the practices, methods and acts which, in the exercise
of reasonable judgment in light of the facts known at the time the decision was
made, could have been expected to accomplish the desired result at a reasonable
cost consistent with good business practices, reliability, safety and
expedition. GOOD UTILITY PRACTICE is not intended to be limited to the optimum
practice, method or act to the exclusion of all others, but rather to be
acceptable practices, methods or acts generally accepted in the region.
   GOVERNMENTAL AUTHORITY. Federal, state, local or other governmental
regulatory or administrative agency, court, commission, department, board or
other governmental subdivision, legislature, rule-making board, tribunal or
other governmental authority having jurisdiction over the parties, their
respective facilities or the respective services they provide, and exercising
or entitled to exercise any administrative, executive, police or taxing
authority, or power; provided, however, that, such term does not include the
customer or any affiliate thereof.
   INTERCONNECTION APPLICATION. The customer’s request to interconnect a new
generating facility, or to increase the capacity of, or make a material
modification to the operating characteristics of an existing generating
facility that is interconnected with the utility’s electrical system.
   INTERCONNECTION STANDARD. All the provisions of this chapter, and related
forms other documents described in this chapter.
   INVERTER. An apparatus that converts direct current into alternating
current.
   QUALIFYING FACILITY. A generation facility that is a QUALIFYING FACILITY
under 18 C.F.R. part 292, subpart B, and is proposed to be used by an
interconnection customer to generate electricity that operates in parallel with
the electric distribution system or local electric power system. QUALIFYING
FACILITIES that are not generating facilities hereunder may qualify for
interconnection with the town’s utility services under provisions of the Public
Utilities Regulatory Policies Act (PURPA), but the terms and conditions of
interconnection shall be determined on a case-by-case basis.
   SYSTEM UPGRADES. The additions, modifications and upgrades to the town’s
distribution system at or beyond the point of interconnection to the generating
facility and render the transmission service necessary to affect the
interconnection customer’s wholesale sale of electricity in interstate
commerce. Distribution upgrades do not include interconnection facilities.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.02 ELIGIBILITY AND APPLICABILITY.
   (A)   Interconnection to the town’s electrical utility shall be granted only
to new or existing customers in good standing under town’s electric service
schedules.
   (B)   (1)   For eligibility for interconnection to the town’s electrical
utility, a generating facility shall have a rated output 100 kilowatts (kW-DC)
or less.
      (2)   Eligibility of a generating facility with rated output of greater
than 100 kW-DC shall be determined by the town on a case-by-case basis
regarding voltage level of connection, metering and purchase of output.
However, a similar facilities interconnection agreement will be required.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.03 REQUEST.
   (A)   A customer desiring to interconnect a qualifying generating facility
must complete and return to the town an application for interconnection, on
forms provided by the town with payment of a $250 processing fee. The town may
require additional details or clarifications as needed to properly evaluate the
application.
   (B)   The town requires, on behalf of its EWS, that the customer provide the
capability to deliver hourly generator AC output meter readings (net of any
generator auxiliary usage) to the EWS. The customer shall install a meter
socket that meets the EWS’s specification between the inverter and the AC
connection to the customer’s load panel. The town shall have the right to
install such additional metering equipment as it deems necessary for the
collection of data for research purposes, which metering will be furnished and
paid for by the town.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.04 SYSTEM EFFECTS.
   (A)   The town and the EWS will analyze the overall impact of the proposed
generating facility on the transmission and distribution system.
   (B)   Such analysis will be based on good utility practice to determine
thermal effects, voltage fluctuations, power quality, system stability and
other relevant information.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.05 SYSTEM UPGRADES.
   As a result of the above analysis, the town and the EWS will provide the
customer with a cost estimate and projected time frame for any system upgrades
that may be necessary to accommodate the generating facility.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.06 AGREEMENTS.
   Once the customer, the town and EWS have identified and mutually agreed upon
the scope of the overall project, including the generating facility, system
upgrades and estimated costs, the customer and town shall execute the customer-
owned generation facilities interconnection agreement, which will be provided
to customer by the town.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.07 CODES AND PERMITS.
   (A)   The customer shall be responsible for procuring all building,
operating and environmental permits that are required by the town any other
governmental authority having jurisdiction for the type of generating facility
and for the necessary ancillary structures to be installed.
   (B)   The equipment shall meet the standards listed in §
155.16 of this chapter.
   (C)   The construction and facilities shall meet all applicable Building and
Electrical Codes.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.08 CERTIFICATE OF COMPLETION.
   Upon completion of the generating facility and prior to its normal
operation, the customer shall provide a signed copy of the certificate of
completion to the town and the EWS, on forms provided by the town.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.09 NORMAL OPERATIONS.
   The customer may begin normal operation of the generating facility upon
completion of all documentation and receipt of written approval from the town
and the EWS.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.10 CHARACTER OF SERVICE.
   The electrical service provided by the EWS shall be 60 cycles per second (60
Hertz) alternating current (AS) at supply voltage and number of phases that
apply under the town rate schedule and the metering requirements established by
EWS.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.11 CODE REQUIREMENTS.
   The generating facility shall meet all requirements established by the
National Electrical Code (NEC), National Electrical Safety Code (NESC),
Institution of Electrical and Electronics Engineers (IEEE), Underwriters
Laboratories (UL) and Occupational Safety and Health Administration. In
addition, manufacturer’s ownership, operating and maintenance manuals shall be
reviewed and accepted by the customer, the town and the EWS prior to beginning
operation.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.12 GENERATING FACILITY CONTROL AND OPERATION.
   The control system of the generating facility shall comply with all IEEE
specifications and standards, including, but not limited to, the following.
   (A)   Power output control system shall automatically disconnect from town’s
electric utility service source upon loss of service voltage and not reconnect
until service voltage has been restored by the town.
   (B)   Power output control system shall ride through voltage fluctuations,
but shall automatically disconnect from the town’s electric utility service
source if the customer-owned generation voltage fluctuates beyond plus or minus
10%. The customer shall provide adequate protection to prevent damage to the
town’s electrical system from inadvertent over/under voltage conditions
originating in customer’s generating facility and to protect the customer’s
generating facility from inadvertent over/under voltage conditions originating
from the town’s electrical system.
   (C)   Power output control system shall ride through frequency fluctuations,
but shall automatically disconnect from town’s electric utility service if
frequency fluctuates beyond plus or minus two cycles per second from 60 cycles
per second (Hertz).
   (D)   Inverter output distortion shall meet IEEE requirements.
   (E)   The generating facility shall meet the applicable IEEE standards
concerning impacts to the distribution system with regard to harmonic
distortion, voltage flicker, power factor, direct current injection and
electromagnetic interference.
   (F)   The voltage produced by the customer’s generating facility must be
balanced if it is a three-phase installation. The customer is responsible for
protecting the generating facility from an inadvertent phase unbalance in the
town’s electric utility service voltage.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.13 FAULT CURRENT CONTRIBUTION.
   The generating facility shall be equipped with protective equipment designed
to automatically disconnect during fault current conditions and remain
disconnected until the voltage and frequency have stabilized.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.14 RECLOSING COORDINATION.
   The generating facility shall be coordinated with the distribution system
reclosing devices by disconnecting from the system during the initial de-
energized operation and shall remain disconnected until the voltage and
frequency have stabilized.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.15 DISCONNECT DEVICE.
   A safety disconnect switch shall be installed that is visible and readily
accessible by town’s electric utility service personnel. The switch shall be
capable of being locked in the open position and shall prevent the generator
from supplying power to the distribution system.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)
§ 155.16 STANDARDS FOR INTERCONNECTION, SAFETY AND OPERATING RELIABILITY.
   The interconnection of a generating facility and associated interconnection
equipment to the town’s distribution system shall meet the applicable
provisions of the following publications:
   (A)   ANSI/IEEE 1547-2003 Standard for Interconnecting Distributed Resources
with Electric Power Systems (including use of IEEE 1547.1 testing protocols to
establish conformity). The following standards shall be used as guidance in
applying IEEE 1547:
      (1)   IEEE Std 519-2014, IEEE Recommended Practices and Requirements for
Harmonic Control in Electrical Power Systems; and
      (2)   IEC/TR3 61000-3-7 Assessment of emission limits for fluctuating
loads in MV and HV power systems.
   (B)   State of Colorado Electric Safety Code;
   (C)   ANSI/NFPA 70 (2014), National Electrical Code;
   (D)   OSHA (29 C.F.R. § 1910.269); and
   (E)   Applicable regional transmission organization/independent system
operator or transmission provider tariff, criteria, business practices,
protocols or other governing documents.
(Ord. 2019-1, passed 1-7-2019)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 156.001 ESTABLISHMENT OF DISTRICTS.
   In order to carry out the provisions of this chapter, the town is divided
into the following zoning districts: R-A Residential District; B-A Business
District; and B-B Business District.
(Prior Code, § 17.04.010) (Ord. 95-3, passed - -1995)
§ 156.002 BOUNDARIES.
   The boundaries of these districts are established as shown on a map entitled
“Zoning District Map” of the town dated 10-2-1995, which map is made a part of
this chapter by reference.
(Prior Code, § 17.04.020) (Ord. 95-3, passed - -1995)
§ 156.003 ANNEXED TERRITORY.
   Any territory hereafter annexed to the town shall be in the R-A District
until changed by an amendment to this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 17.04.030) (Ord. 95-3, passed - -1995)
§ 156.004 APPLICATION OF REGULATIONS.
   Except as otherwise provided, no buildings or other structure or land shall
be used, and no building or other structure shall be erected, reconstructed,
moved into or within the town limits, or structurally altered, except in
conformance with the regulations specified in this chapter for the district in
which said building is located.
(Prior Code, § 17.04.010) (Ord. 95-3, passed - -1995) Penalty, see §
156.999
§ 156.005 ZONING MAP.
